{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","title":"MSCHF drops tiny action figures of your favorite failed startup hardware","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2176032","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Hardware is hard. You can browse the archives of this site and come up with dozens of bold attempts to make new consumer electronics gadgets work &#8212; some of them </span><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2009/11/30/crunchpad-end/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">very close to home</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. But, like all startups, most hardware companies run into the hard-core grind of turning atoms into something worth buying. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To commemorate the hardness of hardware, idea factory/art house MSCHF is releasing a set of five </span><a href=\"https://deadstartuptoys.com/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Dead Startup Toys as vinyl figurines</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> that you can buy for $39.99 each or $159.99 for the set. It bills these as &#8220;iconic failed startups&#8221; and the sales site offers a brief history of the rise and fall of each endeavor. They range from products that never really existed, like the Theranos minilab, to poorly timed early movers like Jibo, to exercises in over-engineering like Juicero. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Given that I have spent much of my career absorbing and trying to understand the difficult and complicated process of bringing consumer hardware to market, I love these things. There could be a lens of malice here, but I choose not to see it that way. Fraud is fraud and the people behind Theranos and debacles like the Coolest Cooler have or will see the business end of the legal system. </span></p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">But big visions and hardware dreams are not always so clearly pocketed into the hole of &#8220;failure.&#8221; Sometimes the hardware works but the supply chain doesn’t. Sometimes the vision is sound but the product is just too early. There are any number of reasons products fail &#8212; but (in as much as they were actually real) you often have to give it up for the teams of people and visionaries that wanted a thing to exist in the universe and dragged it kicking and screaming to that point. And off the cliffs.</span></p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2176034\" style=\"width: 1210px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/003.4f787ee.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2176034\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2176034 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/003.4f787ee.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1200\" height=\"703\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/003.4f787ee.jpg 1200w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/003.4f787ee.jpg?resize=150,88 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/003.4f787ee.jpg?resize=300,176 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/003.4f787ee.jpg?resize=768,450 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/003.4f787ee.jpg?resize=680,398 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/003.4f787ee.jpg?resize=50,29 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2176034\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> <span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">MSCHF</span></p></div></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The figures themselves are really well done, with crisp stamping and accurate detailing with readable text and nicely printed logos. Some of them are articulated as well, and accessorized. The Coolest Cooler gets its infamous blender and the Juicero has a removable (proprietary of course) &#8220;fresh veg&#8221; pouch. The quality on these is quite high overall; I’d rank them up with some of the better novelty toys I’ve bought over the years &#8212; it’s not phoned in, much like the Cooler’s feature set.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The packaging, too, is quite impressive; each gets a customized box and the big set of all of them comes in a bigger rack box. Each one also comes with a &#8220;cause of death&#8221; on the back that tells you why each venture went under. MSCHF went the lengths to make this a pretty premium &#8220;toy&#8221; drop, which is only fitting, given that it’s a monument to physical products. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">As with much of MSCHF’s work, there’s an element of &#8220;wait, is this legal?&#8221; as well, because there are likely a bunch of holes that the IP connected to these products fell into but some of those holes could still have legal entities attached. But that element of danger is what has made many of its projects resonate so far. so I don’t think they’re worried. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">After all, none of these products have the </span><a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/08/style/satan-shoe-settlement-nike.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">sign of the beast on them</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Physically, anyway. (<strong>Image Credits:</strong> MSCHF)</span></p>\n<p>[gallery ids=\"2176106,2176121,2176107,2176105,2176096,2176086,2176090,2176099,2176072,2176079,2176066,2176068,2176071,2176053,2176051,2176058\"]</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote Panzarino","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/003.4f787ee.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn7@2020_2/2021/07/12/18-35-19-567_2ae2aea6ad31d674.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn20@2020_5/2021/07/12/18-35-19-302_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn20@2020_6/2021/07/12/18-37-22-668_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=vrlQ4FmOTKI:nF58T--68ws:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn29@2020_3/2021/07/12/18-37-22-486_5c2ddfcfc3508d87.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=vrlQ4FmOTKI:nF58T--68ws:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn95@2020_6/2021/07/12/18-37-22-963_43b7668b89aea3c6.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/vrlQ4FmOTKI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn41@2020_5/2021/07/12/18-37-22-387_46de42cadb736088.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626114919067},{"createdTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","title":"Ex-SafeBoda executive Babajide Duroshola joins M-KOPA to lead expansion into Nigeria","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2175939","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">On June 18, Babajide Duroshola, ex-country head, SafeBoda Nigeria, <a href=\"https://babajiide.medium.com/and-its-curtains-call-755735f71ca3\">stepped down</a> from his role two years after taking the job post-Andela</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Less than a month later, the executive has found a new role as general manager for Kenyan company M-KOPA</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">His appointment coincides with M-KOPA&#8217;s broader expansion strategy, which includes a move to Nigeria</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In 2019 when SafeBoda hired Duroshola, the Ugandan ride-hailing company was in the news for its imminent expansion to Nigeria</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. To the company, and most of the public, Lagos was the obvious option. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">But Duroshola and his on the ground team chose to stay away from one of Africa&#8217;s most viable tech ecosystems and launch in neighbouring city Ibadan</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Although it </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was considered</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> a huge risk, the gamble looks to have paid off. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While major ride-hailing platforms in Lagos like ORide, MAX.ng and Gokada completely halted their operations in the state after a ride-hailing ban, SafeBoda thrived in Ibadan</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">By the time Duroshola left the company, it had onboarded 5,000 drivers and completed more than 1.5 million rides in a full year of operation</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"cmn1mpyWzn\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/05/11/the-motorcycle-ride-hailing-wars-in-nigeria-and-uganda-is-safebodas-to-lose/\">The motorcycle ride-hailing wars in Nigeria and Uganda are SafeBoda&#8217;s to lose</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;The motorcycle ride-hailing wars in Nigeria and Uganda are SafeBoda&#8217;s to lose&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/05/11/the-motorcycle-ride-hailing-wars-in-nigeria-and-uganda-is-safebodas-to-lose/embed/#?secret=cmn1mpyWzn\" data-secret=\"cmn1mpyWzn\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">SafeBoda runs an asset-financing model when offering smartphones to its riders</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. M-KOPA has used t</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">his concept since its inception and it</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> played a major role in Duroshola&#8217;s decision to join the company.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8220;Part of the things that excite me asides from ride-hailing is the credit space. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I like asking questions on how to extend credits to people and help them build their digital footprints</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. That was why M-KOPA seemed attractive,&#8221; Duroshola told TechCrunch. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">M-KOPA launched in Kenya 10 years ago. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The company </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">is known</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> to have kickstarted the wider pay-as-you-go (PAYG) solar market in the country</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Over the years, M-KOPA has expanded its offerings to include televisions, fridges, other electronic appliances and financial services for customers in Kenya and Uganda</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Through its pay-as-you-go financing model, customers can build ownership over time by paying an initial deposit followed by flexible and affordable micro-payments</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">So far, M-KOPA has sold more than 1 million PAYG solar systems and provided $400 million in financing to millions of customers while raising over $180 million in equity and debt</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Last year, the company added <a href=\"https://technext.ng/2020/01/29/m-kopa-partners-safaricom-samsung-to-roll-out-a-pay-as-you-go-mobile-phone-plan-in-kenya/\">smartphone financing to its offerings</a> in Kenya by partnering with Safaricom and Samsung</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Per a <a href=\"https://www.gsma.com/mobileeconomy/sub-saharan-africa/\">GSMA report</a>, mobile technologies and services generated 9% of sub-Saharan Africa&#8217;s GDP in 2019, representing about $155 billion in economic value</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">And when you think about it, smartphones </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">are used</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> in people&#8217;s everyday lives more than solar systems, so it isn&#8217;t surprising that M-KOPA has already sold 500,000 smartphones, half the units solar systems have managed in a 10-year period.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Earlier this year, M-KOPA ran a pilot test in the Nigerian market by providing customers with its solar systems and smartphone financing options</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Smartphone financing had a higher uptake as M-KOPA sold over 20,000 devices in Lagos, its first market. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The company considered this a success, and the appointment of Duroshola is seen as a prerequisite for </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">scaling the offering rapidly in Nigeria.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8220;We’ve been deliberate about finding the right person with a strong track record and in-depth knowledge of the Nigerian tech community to lead our team as we scale up our country operations. And the milestone coincided with Babajide’s appointment as we look to grow and expand into new regions,&#8221; Mayur Patel, M-KOPA&#8217;s CCO, told TechCrunch in an email.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">M-KOPA is now present in both Lagos and Oyo after expanding to the latter last month. Just as in Kenya, </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">M-KOPA partnered with Samsung, but a different mobile network operator in Airtel, to make its smartphone financing accessible to Nigerian customers. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to Patel, both Nokia and Samsung provide entry-level and mid-tier handsets at different prices to their customers</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. He argues that a top priority for MNOs on the continent is converting 2G/3G network users to 4G. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To him, M-KOPA has a shot at tackling the challenge of 4G device affordability in Nigeria because 75% of its total customers are first-time 4G smartphone owners</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"t573sHF7hh\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/07/25/africas-ride-hail-markets-are-hot-spots-for-startups-and-vc/\">Africa&#8217;s ride-hail markets are hot spots for startups and VC</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Africa&#8217;s ride-hail markets are hot spots for startups and VC&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/07/25/africas-ride-hail-markets-are-hot-spots-for-startups-and-vc/embed/#?secret=t573sHF7hh\" data-secret=\"t573sHF7hh\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8220;Our partnership with both these OEMs has allowed M-KOPA to offer affordable ownership of quality 4G smartphones for underbanked customers, who are otherwise excluded because they lack credit histories or salaried incomes,&#8221; he said</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p>\n<p>In Nigeria, M-KOPA deals with various products in the Samsung A series (A02, A12, A22, A32) ranging from $80-$250 (~₦40,000 to ₦125,000). <span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The company plans to include more devices and handset manufacturers, but the COO doesn&#8217;t say when</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In Kenya and Uganda, however, M-KOPA sells Nokia phones in addition to the aforementioned Samsung products.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Although M-KOPA is focused on smartphone financing in the West African country, Duroshola wants to mirror what Kenyan M-KOPA&#8217;s customers enjoy (where other products asides from smartphones are sold) in Nigeria</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. He reckons it will help build their credit history and worthiness over time.  </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Kenyan company is currently recruiting for engineering roles in Nigeria and globally as part of its expansion plans</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Duroshola will lead the charge in Nigeria in what can be described as his</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> third stint of scaling African startups in the country</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. He seems to have a knack for it. Judging from our conversation, there&#8217;s an optimistic feel about the general manager in his ability to take on a market where PAYG models outside solar systems have had relatively low success.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“My vision as a person and what </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">really</span> <span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">typically</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> drives me on a normal day is to help African startups scale and being that person that would help build, set up, get to the point where they&#8217;re able to think about their business strategy and how they can plug into the Nigerian space. What I&#8217;m looking to build with M-KOPA is a full credit machine. I want it to become a household name within the Nigerian market space where when people are thinking about pay-as-you-go financing for everyday use cases, M-KOPA is what comes to their mind.” </span></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"jpkpX6o5lb\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2016/04/28/solar-startup-m-kopa-leapfrogs-africas-electricity-grid/\">Solar startup M-KOPA leapfrogs Africa&#8217;s electricity grid</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe 02:35:19","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","title":"The Station: Rimac-Bugatti is born, Tesla releases FSD beta v9 and Ola raises $500M","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2175935","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Hello and welcome to The Station, your central hub for all past, present and future means of moving people and packages from Point A to Point B.</p> \n<p>I’m back from my road trip and I am swimming in emails. If you sent me a message on Twitter, email or pigeon post, please give me a few days to dig out of the pile that awaits me.</p> \n<p>You might recall that I mentioned I was off to do some backpacking and climbing in Grand Teton National Park and then eventually would make it to Yellowstone National Park. Yes, the crowds were real, especially for those who stuck to the traditional schedule of sightseeing between 9 a.m. and 5 p.m. I took the early morning and late evening approach and never encountered the infamous parking lot traffic jams.</p>\n<div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div> \n<p>It’s that tactic that allowed me to take a ride in an empty T.E.D.D.Y., the autonomous vehicle that is being piloted in Yellowstone this summer. Beep, in partnership with Local Motors, is operating the autonomous shuttle called T.E.D.D.Y., which stands for The Electric Driverless Demonstration in Yellowstone. The company plans to operate two routes, seven days a week. Information collected during the pilot will be used to inform future deployments in national parks across the country.</p> \n<p>Here’s what I discovered. The two shuttles, which always have a human operator who can take manual control if needed, are currently shuttling folks around the busy Canyons section of the park, specifically between the lodging area and main shopping area, where there is a general store, post office and eateries. The folks operating the shuttle told me about 1,240 people a week are riding the TEDDY vehicles and that riders were both curious and more knowledgeable about the tech than they expected.</p> \n<p>My ride was uneventful, as it should have been. The vehicle did pause unnecessarily because the self-driving system thought it needed to. The human safety operator warned me that this pause would likely occur, as it had been happening regularly over the past few days.</p> \n<p>One final item. <a href=\"https://twitter.com/theautonocast?lang=en\">The Autonocast</a>, the podcast I co-host with Alex Roy and Ed Niedermeyer, is teaming up with SAE for a zoom call to have a wide-ranging discussion on the future of transportation and how the discourse about autonomous vehicle technology that occurs online — yes, Twitter I’m looking at you — impacts public perception. Specifically, we’re going to dig into a term coined by <a href=\"https://twitter.com/lizadixon?ref_src=twsrc%5Egoogle%7Ctwcamp%5Eserp%7Ctwgr%5Eauthor\">Liza Dixon</a> called “autonowashing.</p> \n<p>SAE MidCal, in conjunction with SAE SoCal, is hosting the meeting, which you can <a href=\"https://saesocal-org.zoom.us/webinar/register/WN_vbQaj2qCSEyZLLt9bab7dw\">register for here</a>. Please join us and post your questions in advance to get the conversation started.</p> \n<p>As always, you can email me at <a href=\"mailto:kirsten.korosec@techcrunch.com\">kirsten.korosec@techcrunch.com</a> to share thoughts, criticisms, opinions or tips. You also can send a direct message to me at Twitter — <a href=\"https://twitter.com/kirstenkorosec\">@kirstenkorosec</a>.</p> \n<h2>Micromobbin’</h2> \n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/the-station-scooter1.png\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone wp-image-1999054 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/the-station-scooter1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1600\" height=\"401\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/the-station-scooter1.png 1600w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/the-station-scooter1.png?resize=150,38 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/the-station-scooter1.png?resize=300,75 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/the-station-scooter1.png?resize=768,192 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/the-station-scooter1.png?resize=680,170 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/the-station-scooter1.png?resize=1536,385 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/the-station-scooter1.png?resize=50,13 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1600px) 100vw, 1600px\" /></a></p> \n<p>With many people blissfully still on holiday after the Fourth of July weekend, it was a slow week in the micromobility universe. One thing that did catch my eye though was an announcement from Stockholm-based e-scooter operator <strong>Voi</strong> that it launched the “world’s first large scale pilot of computer vision on e-scooters” using Irish computer vision startup Luna’s technology.</p> \n<p>Now, I’m not quite sure what Voi means by “at scale” since the press release had no mention of how many of these scooters the company would be bringing to its pilot beginning this month in Northampton, U.K. However, the release did make reference to Luna’s AI models getting more accurate by using data captured from 100 cameras on e-scooters in the English city, so that’s at least 100 scooters. The problem is, Voi is by no means the first. Spin beat them to the punch.</p> \n<p>Last month, Ford-owned <strong>Spin</strong> launched its <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/06/03/ford-owned-spin-shakes-up-scooter-business-with-new-ceo-e-bikes-and-city-strategy/\">Spin Insight Level 2</a> — its bundle of sensors, cameras and on-board computing power to detect sidewalk- and bike-lane riding and validate parking from its partner Drover AI — with 100 e-scooters in Milwaukee. Spin also has some computer vision-enabled scooters in Santa Monica, where it just launched, and will be bringing them to Seattle and Miami in the coming months.</p> \n<div class=\"embed breakout\"> \n <blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"oZDJaDel2v\">\n  <p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/06/03/ford-owned-spin-shakes-up-scooter-business-with-new-ceo-e-bikes-and-city-strategy/\">Ford-owned Spin shakes up scooter business with new CEO, e-bikes and city strategy</a></p>\n </blockquote> \n <p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"“Ford-owned Spin shakes up scooter business with new CEO, e-bikes and city strategy” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/06/03/ford-owned-spin-shakes-up-scooter-business-with-new-ceo-e-bikes-and-city-strategy/embed/#?secret=oZDJaDel2v\" data-secret=\"oZDJaDel2v\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></p>\n</div> \n<h3>BMW is finally producing its electric scooter</h3> \n<p><strong>BMW’s</strong> <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/07/bmw-is-finally-producing-its-retro-futuristic-ce-04-electric-scooter-but-at-12k-will-anyone-buy-it/\">new electric scooter</a> is very cool-looking, with a retro-futuristic vibe and a low to the ground ride. But it ain’t cheap. At $12,000, is anyone gonna buy this thing? I guess we’ll find out. The first scooter actually produced from the Motorrad Concept Link series will be part of BMW’s 2022 lineup.</p> \n<h3>More electric scooter news …</h3> \n<p>Indian ride-hailing company <strong>Ola</strong> has announced its giant e-scooter facility is ready and will soon begin production, with an expected launch this month. Late last year, the company invested $327 million to set it up, so we’ll potentially see the fruits of that investment. Apparently, Ola Electric has 3,000 robots building a scooter every two minutes, and the factory has 10 production lines, bringing total production capacity to about 10 million e-scooters.</p> \n<p>According to a <a href=\"https://www.acutemarketreports.com/report/electric-kick-scooters-market\">new report</a> by <strong>Acute Market Reports</strong>, electric kick scooters are expected to reach a market volume of 1.4 million units by 2028. The analysis found kick scooters are getting more popular as more people try to avoid public transportation, and that there’s a growing demand for longer-range scooters for heavy usage. The report identified some of the key manufacturers of electric kick scooters to be Razor USA LLC, GOTRAX, Xiaomi, Segway, Inc., ZERO Electric Scooters, MINIMOTORS Co., Ltd., Kaabo Electric Scooter, Titan Group, Glion and SWAGTRON.</p> \n<p><strong>Helbiz</strong>, a micromobility operator that recently went SPAC by merging with GreenVision Acquisition Corp., has <a href=\"https://finance.yahoo.com/news/helbiz-partners-irengo-telepass-launch-120000016.html\">announced a partnership</a> with IrenGo and Telepass to deploy 50 MiMoto electric mopeds throughout the Italian cities of Portofino, Santa Margherita Ligure, Rapallo, Paraggi and Punta Pedale. Hellbiz is the first and only operator in this region.</p> \n<h3>What’s a newsletter without a hint of Lime</h3> \n<p><strong>Lime’s</strong> e-bikes are officially in <a href=\"https://www.wkyc.com/article/news/local/cleveland/lime-e-bikes-now-available-downtown-cleveland/95-5ada4947-9822-4f42-94dc-1c7d516d7f17\">downtown Cleveland</a> after the city issued permits allowing the bikes this year. The company started with 50 but will add more soon. Lime’s bikes will also be accompanied by more from Spin and Bird.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: right;\"><em>— Rebecca Bellan</em></p> \n<h2>Deal of the week</h2> \n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/money-the-station.png\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone wp-image-1896226 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/money-the-station.png\" alt=\"money the station\" width=\"1600\" height=\"400\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/money-the-station.png 1600w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/money-the-station.png?resize=150,38 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/money-the-station.png?resize=300,75 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/money-the-station.png?resize=768,192 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/money-the-station.png?resize=680,170 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/money-the-station.png?resize=1536,384 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/money-the-station.png?resize=50,13 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1600px) 100vw, 1600px\" /></a></p> \n<p>The deal I’ve been waiting for is finally done. <strong>Rimac Automobili</strong>, the Porsche-backed Croatian company that makes electric hypercars and components for automakers, is <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/05/vw-offloads-bugatti-to-rimac-to-form-new-ev-company-bugatti-rimac/\">taking over <strong>Bugatti</strong></a>. Rimac will own a controlling 55% share in the new company, Bugatti-Rimac, with VW’s Porsche owning the remaining 45%.</p> \n<p>A few nuts and bolts on the deal: Rimac is going to separate the development, production and supply of battery systems, drivetrains and other EV components into a new entity owned by Rimac Group called Rimac Technology, which will work independently with other global car manufacturers.</p> \n<p>Founder Mate Rimac will continue to hold his 37% share in Rimac Group, with Hyundai Motor Group holding the same 12% and other investors at 27%. Porsche recently upped its stake in Rimac from 15% to 24%, but its total ownership doesn’t give it a controlling interest in the new EV company. Mate Rimac will lead Bugatti-Rimac, which will be headquartered in Zagreb, Croatia. Bugatti’s manufacturing will remain in Molsheim, France.</p> \n<p>Mate Rimac was on our virtual stage in June and talked about the company’s future plans, including confirming that they were in talks with Bugatti. Extra Crunch members can watch the <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/video/building-an-electric-powerhouse/\">entire interview</a> or <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/06/29/rimac-automobili-founder-mate-rimac-shares-lessons-from-bootstrapping-an-ev-company/\">read a recap here</a>.</p> \n<div class=\"embed breakout\"> \n <blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"CPLF3wlNV9\">\n  <p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/06/29/rimac-automobili-founder-mate-rimac-shares-lessons-from-bootstrapping-an-ev-company/\">Rimac Automobili founder Mate Rimac shares lessons from bootstrapping an EV company</a></p>\n </blockquote> \n <p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"“Rimac Automobili founder Mate Rimac shares lessons from bootstrapping an EV company” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/06/29/rimac-automobili-founder-mate-rimac-shares-lessons-from-bootstrapping-an-ev-company/embed/#?secret=CPLF3wlNV9\" data-secret=\"CPLF3wlNV9\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></p>\n</div> \n<p><strong>Other deals that caught my eye as I emerge from vacation mode …</strong></p> \n<p><strong>Kurly</strong>, a South Korean startup that provides next-day grocery delivery services across the country, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/09/kurly-the-korean-grocery-startup-raises-200m-on-a-2-2b-valuation-after-shifting-ipo-plans-away-from-the-nyse/\">raised $200 million</a> in funding in a Series F valuing the company at $2.2 billion. The company’s valuation has more than doubled in the last year. Last April, Kurly closed a Series E of $150 million at a $780 million valuation.</p> \n<p><strong>Lacuna Technologies</strong>, a startup that helps cities create and enforce transportation policies by building and managing open-source digital tools, has <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/07/lacuna-raises-16-million-in-series-a-to-help-cities-manage-mobility-via-digital-twin/\">raised $16 million</a> in a Series A round, bringing the company’s total investment to $33.5 million. The round was led by Xplorer Capital Management, and includes Playground Global, the company’s founding investor. Participating investors include JetBlue Technology Ventures and Lauder Partners. Along with the funding news Lacuna is announcing the addition of Keith Nilsson, MP and co-founder of Xplorer, to the company’s board.</p> \n<p><strong>MaxAB</strong>, an Egyptian startup based out of Cairo that serves a network of traditional food and grocery retailers across Egypt, has <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/05/maxab-the-egyptian-b2b-food-and-grocery-delivery-startup-raises-40m-for-expansion/\">raised $40 million</a> in Series A financing.</p> \n<p><strong>Ola</strong>, the Indian ride-hailing giant, is flush with <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/08/temasek-and-warburg-pincus-invest-500-million-in-ola/\">$500 million in new capital</a> thanks to investments from Temasek and an affiliate of Warburg Pincus. Ola co-founder and chief executive Bhavish Aggarwal is also participating in the new investment, the startup said. Ola said in a statement that the investment comes “ahead of IPO” — but didn’t elaborate.</p> \n<p><strong>Stellantis</strong>, the global automaker born out of a merger between Fiat Chrysler Automobiles and French automaker Groupe PSA, will <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/08/auto-giant-stellantis-to-invest-e30b-in-electrification-through-2025/\">invest €30 billion</a> ($35.5 billion) in electric vehicles and new software over the next four years as part of a major push to transition away from internal combustion engines. Stellantis shared a few of its plans, including manufacturing an electric Dodge muscle car and an electric Ram pickup truck by 2024. Stellantis also said it would offer an electric or plug-in model in every vehicle segment under its Jeep brand by 2025.</p> \n<p><strong>Volvo Group</strong>, <strong>Daimler Truck</strong> and Volkswagen’s AG heavy-truck business the <strong>Traton Group </strong>plan to<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/05/volvo-daimler-traton-invest-593-million-to-build-electric-truck-charging-network/\"> invest €500 million</a> (~$593 million USD) to install and operate 1,700 charging points in strategic locations and close to highways&nbsp;for electric heavy-duty long-haul trucks and buses around Europe.&nbsp;The automakers intend to finalize the agreement by the end of this year and start operations next year, with the hopes of increasing the number of charge points significantly as the companies seek additional partners for the future joint venture.</p> \n<div class=\"embed breakout\"> \n <blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"12OLNNnHo4\">\n  <p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/05/volvo-daimler-traton-invest-593-million-to-build-electric-truck-charging-network/\">Volvo, Daimler, Traton invest $593 million to build electric truck charging network</a></p>\n </blockquote> \n <p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"“Volvo, Daimler, Traton invest $593 million to build electric truck charging network” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/05/volvo-daimler-traton-invest-593-million-to-build-electric-truck-charging-network/embed/#?secret=12OLNNnHo4\" data-secret=\"12OLNNnHo4\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></p>\n</div> \n<p><strong>Zomato</strong>, a food delivery startup in India that competes with Swiggy, has boosted its <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/08/zomato-ipo/\">plan to raise $1.3 billion</a> in its initial public offering, which opens on July 14 and closes July 16. Zomato said it will price its shares in the range of 72 Indian rupees (96 cents) to 76 ($1) and is targeting an upper limit valuation of $8.56 billion.&nbsp;It plans to list on Indian stock exchanges.</p> \n<h2>Policy corner</h2> \n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/the-station-delivery.png\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone wp-image-2037863 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/the-station-delivery.png\" alt=\"the-station-delivery\" width=\"1600\" height=\"401\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/the-station-delivery.png 1600w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/the-station-delivery.png?resize=150,38 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/the-station-delivery.png?resize=300,75 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/the-station-delivery.png?resize=768,192 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/the-station-delivery.png?resize=680,170 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/the-station-delivery.png?resize=1536,385 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/the-station-delivery.png?resize=50,13 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1600px) 100vw, 1600px\" /></a></p> \n<p>Welcome back to Policy Corner! The big news this week comes from across the Atlantic, where European lawmakers are planning to introduce a ban on the sale of new internal combustion engine vehicles by 2035.</p> \n<p>Yep — less than 15 years from now. The ban would be phased in; countries would first be required to drop emissions from new vehicles by 65% by 2030, according to a document from the European Commission that was <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-07-09/europe-to-propose-end-of-combustion-engine-era-in-green-overhaul\">viewed by Bloomberg</a>. The ruling would accompany a larger set of procedures for lowering greenhouse gas emissions across sectors, with the overall aim of reaching net-zero emissions on the continent by 2050.</p> \n<p>News of a 2035 ban has been floating around for a while, but it seems that we’re now approaching the introduction of the proposal on July 14. Nor will it likely shock automakers, many of whom have been announcing their own ambitious zero-emissions targets. Fiat and Volvo have both set their own ICE phase outs in the continent by the end of the decade, for example. Volvo, along with Uber, also <a href=\"https://icephaseout.org/\">signed a letter in support</a> of the ban in April.</p> \n<p>If the ban is included in the final proposal, it would still need to be approved by European Commissioners before going into effect. We’ll be keeping our eyes out for that final proposal — I’m especially interested to see if it will include any mandates for installing EV chargers or other rulings to help spur the transition toward electric mobility. While many EU countries have already set electrification targets separate from the proposed mandate, auto-making remains a cornerstone of the economy in countries like France and Germany. Whatever ends up happening, it’ll likely be expensive.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: right;\"><em>— Aria Alamalhodaei</em></p> \n<h2>Notable reads and other tidbits</h2> \n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/the-station-ride-hailing1.png\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone wp-image-1926823 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/the-station-ride-hailing1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1600\" height=\"401\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/the-station-ride-hailing1.png 1600w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/the-station-ride-hailing1.png?resize=150,38 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/the-station-ride-hailing1.png?resize=300,75 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/the-station-ride-hailing1.png?resize=768,192 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/the-station-ride-hailing1.png?resize=680,170 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/the-station-ride-hailing1.png?resize=1536,385 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/the-station-ride-hailing1.png?resize=50,13 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1600px) 100vw, 1600px\" /></a></p> \n<p>A short week + vacation means this won’t be as long as usual. (At least for me.) Let’s dig in.</p> \n<h3>Autonomous vehicles</h3> \n<p><strong>Yandex Self-Driving Group</strong>, a unit of the publicly traded Russian tech giant, is <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/06/yandex-self-driving-group-partners-with-grubhub-to-bring-robotic-delivery-to-college-campuses/\">partnering with food delivery service GrubHub</a> to be its multiyear robotic delivery provider across American college campuses. Yandex hopes to reach more than 250 campuses over the course of this partnership, beginning with dozens of robots in the fall, according to Yandex Self-Driving CEO Dmitry Polishchuk.</p> \n<div class=\"embed breakout\"> \n <blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"jXDuZFo6cj\">\n  <p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/06/yandex-self-driving-group-partners-with-grubhub-to-bring-robotic-delivery-to-college-campuses/\">Yandex Self-Driving Group partners with GrubHub to bring robotic delivery to college campuses</a></p>\n </blockquote> \n <p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"“Yandex Self-Driving Group partners with GrubHub to bring robotic delivery to college campuses” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/06/yandex-self-driving-group-partners-with-grubhub-to-bring-robotic-delivery-to-college-campuses/embed/#?secret=jXDuZFo6cj\" data-secret=\"jXDuZFo6cj\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></p>\n</div> \n<h3>Electric vehicles</h3> \n<p><strong>Bentley Motors</strong> revealed its <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/06/bentley-reveals-flying-spur-hybrid-its-latest-in-the-push-towards-electric/\">newest hybrid model</a> that is<span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\"> part of the company’s Beyond100 plan to become a carbon-neutral organization with an entirely electrified range by 2023 and a totally electric lineup by 2030. As Rebecca Bellan noted, that’s a tall order, given the fact that the British company’s first all-electric vehicle isn’t expected to come to market until 2025. So far, Bentley only has this hybrid and another, the Bentayga SUV.</span></p> \n<p><strong>Tesla</strong> has started the long-promised updates for its “Full Self-Driving” Beta v9 software. This is not full self-driving, which is why this item is housed under “electric vehicles.” Instead, this is an advanced driver assist system. But it’s important because this is the first “feature complete” version of the so-called FSD. This version also only relies on cameras and doesn’t include radar, a sensor that was previously used by Tesla’s advanced driver assistance system.</p> \n<p>There are already a bunch of <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7NW6mICjUvM&amp;t=1128s\">videos</a> popping up on the beta V9 FSD. And while many folks are excited to have early access, what struck me was the numerous disengagements I viewed during these videoed drives. Check out this one on <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OrHCz4wnW8g\">unprotected left-hand turns</a>.</p> \n<h3>Other stuff</h3> \n<p>The <strong>European Union&nbsp;</strong><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/08/eu-fines-bmw-vw-1b-for-running-emissions-cartel-since-the-90s/\">issued fines of $1 billion</a> (€875 million) to<strong> Volkswagen</strong> and <strong>BMW</strong> &nbsp;for their involvement in an emissions cartel. According to the EU, Volkswagen, Audi, Porsche, BMW and Mercedes-Benz parent company Daimler have been illegally colluding to restrict competition in emission cleaning for new diesel passenger cars, essentially slowing the deployment of cleaner emissions tech.</p> \n<p><strong>Halo</strong>, the Las Vegas-based startup, is launching a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/08/halo-will-launch-a-remotely-operated-car-service-powered-by-5g-in-las-vegas/\">remotely operated electric car service</a> powered by 5G. This is starting as a pilot with just five vehicles. Halo users can order a vehicle via an app. Once a vehicle is ordered, a remote operator will drive it to the waiting customer. The user takes delivery and then manually operates the vehicle until they’re done. When the trip is complete, the remote operator takes back over and drives it to the next waiting customer. The pilot is being conducted in partnership with T-Mobile.</p> \n<div class=\"embed breakout\"> \n <blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"RNgXj8Tm34\">\n  <p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/08/halo-will-launch-a-remotely-operated-car-service-powered-by-5g-in-las-vegas/\">Halo will launch a remotely operated car service powered by 5G in Las Vegas</a></p>\n </blockquote> \n <p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"“Halo will launch a remotely operated car service powered by 5G in Korosec","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/the-station-scooter1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn14@2020_5/2021/07/12/18-35-19-359_1f46672f108f4ca5.webp","https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/money-the-station.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn27@2020_2/2021/07/12/18-37-22-497_bd3f01dd0a54a1d6.webp","https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/the-station-delivery.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn73@2020_3/2021/07/12/18-37-22-760_f13db4cccd5400f3.webp","https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/the-station-ride-hailing1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn92@2020_4/2021/07/12/18-37-23-182_8b753053b307bebd.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn20@2020_5/2021/07/12/18-35-19-302_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn20@2020_6/2021/07/12/18-37-22-668_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=xwQIQtb1eYs:47fdycMZ2Bg:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn54@2020_5/2021/07/12/18-37-22-581_fb2344670e96ec17.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=xwQIQtb1eYs:47fdycMZ2Bg:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn39@2020_4/2021/07/12/18-37-23-055_1b116f8f0d781319.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/xwQIQtb1eYs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn76@2020_5/2021/07/12/18-37-22-885_e7e3ba3d557e5609.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626114919070},{"createdTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","title":"Controversial WhatsApp policy change hit with consumer law complaint in Europe","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2175968","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Facebook has been accused of multiple breaches of European Union consumer protection law as a result of its attempts to force WhatsApp users to accept controversial changes to the messaging platforms&#8217; terms of use &#8212; such as threatening users that the app would stop working if they did not accept the updated policies by May 15.</p>\n<p>The consumer protection association umbrella group, the Beuc, <a href=\"https://www.beuc.eu/publications/consumer-groups-file-complaint-against-whatsapp-unfairly-pressuring-users-accept-its/html\">said today</a> that together with eight of its member organizations it&#8217;s filed a complaint with the European Commission and with the European network of consumer authorities.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The complaint is first due to the persistent, recurrent and intrusive notifications pushing users to accept WhatsApp’s policy updates,&#8221; it wrote in a press release.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>&#8220;The content of these notifications, their nature, timing and recurrence put an undue pressure on users and impair their freedom of choice. As such, they are a breach of the EU Directive on Unfair Commercial Practices.&#8221;</p>\n<p>After earlier telling users that notifications about the need to accept the new policy would become persistent, interfering with their ability to use the service, WhatsApp later <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/05/06/whatsapp-is-doing-fine-despite-months-long-backlash-over-policy-update/\">rowed back from its own draconian deadline</a>.</p>\n<p>However the app continues to bug users to accept the update &#8212; with no option not to do so (users can close the policy prompt but are unable to decline the new terms or stop the app continuing to pop-up a screen asking them to accept the update).</p>\n<p>&#8220;In addition, the complaint highlights the opacity of the new terms and the fact that WhatsApp has failed to explain in plain and intelligible language the nature of the changes,&#8221; the Beuc went on. &#8220;It is basically impossible for consumers to get a clear understanding of what consequences WhatsApp’s changes entail for their privacy, particularly in relation to the transfer of their personal data to Facebook and other third parties. This ambiguity amounts to a breach of EU consumer law which obliges companies to use clear and transparent contract terms and commercial communications.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The organization pointed out that WhatsApp&#8217;s policy updates remain under scrutiny by privacy regulations in Europe &#8212; which it argues is another factor that makes Facebook&#8217;s aggressive attempts to push the policy on users highly inappropriate.</p>\n<p>And while this consumer-law focused complaint is separate to the privacy issues the Beuc also flags &#8212; which are being investigated by EU data protection authorities (DPAs) &#8212; it has called on those regulators to speed up their investigations, adding: &#8220;We urge the European network of consumer authorities and the network of data protection authorities to work in close cooperation on these issues.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The Beuc has produced a <a href=\"https://www.beuc.eu/publications/beuc-x-2021-063_report_-_whats_up_with_whatsapp.pdf\">report</a> setting out its concerns about the WhatsApp ToS change in more detail &#8212; where it hits out at the &#8220;opacity&#8221; of the new policies, further asserting:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;WhatsApp remains very vague about the sections it has removed and the ones it has added. It is up to users to seek out this information by themselves. Ultimately, it is almost impossible for users to clearly understand what is new and what has been amended. The opacity of the new policies is in breach of Article 5 of the UCTD [Unfair Contract Terms Directive] and is also a misleading and unfair practice prohibited under Article 5 and 6 of the UCPD [Unfair Commercial Practices Directive].&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>Reached for comment on the consumer complaint, a WhatsApp spokesperson told us:</p>\n<blockquote><p>“Beuc’s action is based on a misunderstanding of the purpose and effect of the update to our terms of service. Our recent update explains the options people have to message a business on WhatsApp and provides further transparency about how we collect and use data. The update does not expand our ability to share data with Facebook, and does not impact the privacy of your messages with friends or family, wherever they are in the world. We would welcome an opportunity to explain the update to Beuc and to clarify what it means for people.”</p></blockquote>\n<p>The Commission was also contacted for comment on the Beuc&#8217;s complaint &#8212; we&#8217;ll update this report if we get a response.</p>\n<p><strong>Update:</strong> A Commission official told us:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;We have received the alert from the European Consumer Organisation (BEUC) who today filed a complaint against WhatsApp for multiple breaches of EU consumer rights.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The European Commission will carefully consider all the elements brought forward by BEUC together with the national consumer authorities in the coming weeks to assess the need for further investigation into the matter and a possible coordinated action as foreseen under the Consumer protection cooperation (CPC) regulation.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Coordinated actions are regularly conducted by the CPC network whose objective it is to enforce consumer rights consistently across the Single Market.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We expect all companies providing services in the EU to comply with EU data protection rules.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Under the GDPR, supervising and enforcing its rules is the responsibility of the national data protection authorities, where necessary cooperating with the European Data Protection Board.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The Commission is closely following this issue.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>The complaint is just the latest pushback in Europe over the controversial terms change by Facebook-owned WhatsApp &#8212; which triggered a privacy warning from Italy back in <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/01/14/confusion-over-whatsapps-new-tcs-triggers-privacy-warning-from-italy/\">January</a>, followed by an urgency procedure in Germany in <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/05/11/facebook-ordered-not-to-apply-controversial-whatsapp-tcs-in-germany/\">May</a> when Hamburg&#8217;s DPA banned the company from processing additional WhatsApp user data.</p>\n<p>Although, earlier this year, Facebook&#8217;s lead data regulator in the EU, Ireland&#8217;s Data Protection Commission, appeared to accept Facebook&#8217;s reassurances that the ToS changes do not affect users in the region.</p>\n<p>German DPAs were less happy, though. And Hamburg invoked emergency powers allowed for in the General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR) in a bid to circumvent a mechanism in the regulation that (otherwise) funnels cross-border complaints and concerns via a lead regulator &#8212; typically where a data controller has their regional base (in Facebook/WhatsApp&#8217;s case that&#8217;s Ireland).</p>\n<p>Such emergency procedures are time-limited to three months. But the European Data Protection Board (EDPB) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/EU_EDPB/status/1414533127511420928\">confirmed today</a> that its plenary meeting will discuss the Hamburg DPA&#8217;s request for it to make an urgent binding decision &#8212; which could see the Hamburg DPA&#8217;s intervention set on a more lasting footing, depending upon what the EDPB decides.</p>\n<p>In the meanwhile, calls for Europe&#8217;s regulators to work together to better tackle the challenges posed by platform power are growing, with a number of regional competition authorities and privacy regulators actively <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/06/18/perspectives-on-tackling-big-techs-market-power/\">taking steps to dial up their joint working</a> &#8212; in a bid to ensure that expertise across distinct areas of law doesn&#8217;t stay siloed and, thereby, risk disjointed enforcement, with conflicting and contradictory outcomes for Internet users.</p>\n<p>There seems to be a growing understanding on both sides of the Atlantic for a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/09/biden-executive-order-tech-antitrust/\">joined up approach to regulating platform power</a> and ensuring powerful platforms don&#8217;t simply get let off the hook.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"z2FQ6UET98\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/06/18/perspectives-on-tackling-big-techs-market-power/\">Perspectives on tackling Big Tech&#8217;s market power</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe 02:35:19","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","title":"VU raises $12M to remove cybersecurity friction from digital experiences","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2175927","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Pretty soon, people won’t have to provide a fingerprint or a driver license to prove their identity — if <a href=\"https://www.vusecurity.com/en\">VU</a> has its way.</p>\n<p>The Argentina-based fraud and identity protection company announced $12 million in Series B funding Monday from backers including software developer Globant, as well as Agrega Partners, NXTP Ventures, Bridge One, the IDB Lab and Telefónica. The new funding gives the company total venture-backed investments of $20 million, CEO Sebastián Stranieri told TechCrunch.</p>\n<p>Stranieri, who has worked in the cybersecurity industry for the past 20 years, got the idea for VU in 2007 after spending hours helping his grandmother verify her identity with the Argentinian government in what turned out to be a two-minute process.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>“It pushed me to create a company to help create digital experiences without the friction,” he told TechCrunch.</p>\n<p>VU’s technology takes a person’s “online persona” and uses geolocation, biometrics and user behavior analysis to provide identity verification for users and enable a continuous authentication process that sees and connects the users’ online and offline personas. Simply put, it works mainly with government entities in countries like Argentina and Ecuador, providing them a way to confirm if people are who they say they are.</p>\n<p>VU is one of several startups applying technology to fraud and identity within a global digital identity market expected to reach over $33 billion by 2025, according to <a href=\"https://www.globenewswire.com/news-release/2020/07/14/2061673/0/en/Digital-Identity-Solutions-Market-to-grow-at-16-CAGR-to-reach-US-33-billion-by-2025-Global-Insights-on-Top-Trends-Expansion-Plans-Investments-Analysis-Key-Growth-Drivers-Leading-Pl.html\">Adroit Market Research</a>. Companies recently capturing investment dollars for similar technology include Sift, which <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/22/fraud-prevention-platform-sift-raises-50m-at-over-1b-valuation-eyes-acquisitions/\">raised $50 million</a> in April for a valuation of over $1 billion, and <a href=\"https://www.socure.com/\">Socure</a>, which announced <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/16/socure-raises-100m-at-1-3b-valuation-proving-identity-verification-is-hotter-than-ever/\">$100 million in Series D funding</a> at a $1.3 billion valuation.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"WhCFNvMF49\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/16/socure-raises-100m-at-1-3b-valuation-proving-identity-verification-is-hotter-than-ever/\">Socure raises $100M at $1.3B valuation, proving identity verification is hotter than ever</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Socure raises $100M at $1.3B valuation, proving identity verification is hotter than ever&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/16/socure-raises-100m-at-1-3b-valuation-proving-identity-verification-is-hotter-than-ever/embed/#?secret=WhCFNvMF49\" data-secret=\"WhCFNvMF49\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>In the past three years, VU has grown to more than 150 employees and is operating across Latin America and Europe, catering to big name customers like Santander and Prisma, and governments in Latin America. The company also opened its first office in New York, where Stranieri expects to more than quadruple headcount in the next year.</p>\n<p>The company is averaging 85% year over year revenue growth, and he expects that to continue in 2021 with 100% growth forecasted for 2022. In addition to New York, VU opened an office in Madrid and will open offices in Italy, France and the United Kingdom.</p>\n<p>As such, he intends to use the new funding to hire developers across Europe and in the U.S.</p>\n<p>Globant’s investment into VU also serves as a partnership. Globant provides software development to the likes of Google, Disney and Apple. Together, they will package VU’s digital experience so that companies can purchase the basic software and then customize it. Currently, VU’s technology is suited for banks and to provide a one-click e-commerce checkout where a retailer’s system will recognize and confirm the buyer.</p>\n<p>“Globant is changing the digital experience, so having their backing is a great message to our customers and partners that we are performing well,” Stranieri said. “Their backup and those of all of our investors provides an opportunity to take a risk and help us grow faster.”</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"5HmEKWFQPJ\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/06/04/its-time-for-security-teams-to-embrace-security-data-lakes/\">It’s time for security teams to embrace security data lakes</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe id=\"speakable-summary\">Flipkart said on Monday it has raised $3.6 billion at a post-money valuation of $37.6 billion in what is widely believed to be the pre-IPO round for <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/14/walmart-invests-additional-1-2-billion-in-indias-flipkart-to-increase-stake/\">the Indian e-commerce conglomerate</a> as it works to list in the public markets as soon as early next year.</p>\n<p>The new round of funding &#8212; by far the largest for any Indian startup &#8212; was led by GIC, Canada Pension Plan Investment Board (CPP Investments), SoftBank Vision Fund 2 and Walmart, along with investments from sovereign funds DisruptAD, Qatar Investment Authority, Khazanah Nasional Berhad, Tencent, Willoughby Capital, Antara Capital, Franklin Templeton and Tiger Global.</p>\n<p>The Monday investment marks the return of SoftBank as a shareholder of Flipkart. SoftBank, which had taken the exit from the startup when the Bangalore-based firm sold majority stakes to <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/05/09/walmart-confirms-16b-flipkart-investment-giving-it-77-in-indias-e-commerce-leader/\">Walmart in 2018 at a valuation of $22 billion</a>, has reinvested about $500 million in the new round.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>&#8220;At Flipkart, we are committed to transforming the consumer internet ecosystem in India and providing consumers access and value. This investment by leading global investors reflects the promise of digital commerce in India and their belief in Flipkart’s capabilities to maximise this potential for all stakeholders,&#8221; said Kalyan Krishnamurthy, Chief Executive Officer at Flipkart Group, in a statement.</p>\n<p>&#8220;As we serve our consumers, we will focus on accelerating growth for millions of small and medium Indian businesses, including kiranas. We will continue to invest in new categories and leverage made-in-India technology to transform consumer experiences and develop a world-class supply chain.”</p>\n<p>As part of the new fundraise, Flipkart is also giving its employees the option to sell their stock options worth $80.5 million, Krishnamurthy told them on Monday.</p>\n<p>Flipkart had originally hit the market to raise money early this year and was initially looking to <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/05/10/flipkart-in-early-talks-to-raise-1-billion-ahead-of-ipo/\">raise just about $1 billion</a>, TechCrunch first reported.</p>\n<p>The Bangalore-headquartered firm competes neck to neck with Amazon in India. They are also expected to be <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/06/21/india-proposes-tougher-e-commerce-rules-following-widespread-cheating-and-unfair-trade-by-amazon-and-flipkart/\">severely hit by India&#8217;s new e-commerce rules</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"a5ICkENkPI\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/06/21/india-proposes-tougher-e-commerce-rules-following-widespread-cheating-and-unfair-trade-by-amazon-and-flipkart/\">India proposes tougher e-commerce rules to address &#8216;widespread cheating&#8217; complaints</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;India proposes tougher e-commerce rules to address &#8216;widespread cheating&#8217; complaints&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/06/21/india-proposes-tougher-e-commerce-rules-following-widespread-cheating-and-unfair-trade-by-amazon-and-flipkart/embed/#?secret=a5ICkENkPI\" data-secret=\"a5ICkENkPI\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>E-commerce platform JioMart, a joint venture between Reliance Retail (India’s largest retail chain) and Google and Facebook-backed Jio Platforms (India’s largest telecom operator), launched last year in <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/05/23/jiomart-the-e-commerce-venture-by-indias-richest-man-launches-in-additional-cities/\">over 200 cities and towns across the nation</a>.</p>\n<p>At stake is one of the world’s fastest-growing e-commerce markets that is poised to grow even further as more first-time internet users begin to shop online. India’s e-commerce market is estimated to reach more than 300 million shoppers by 2025, according to estimates by Bain &#38; Company. These shoppers would have bought items worth more than $100 billion from online platforms, the firm projected.</p>\n<p>In recent years, Flipkart and Amazon have made a number of bets to expand their reach in India. Both of them have rolled out support for Hindi language (Flipkart has added several additional Indian languages as well), and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/06/26/amazon-launches-smart-stores-in-india-to-win-mom-and-pop/\">partnered with neighborhood stores</a>.</p>\n<p>“Flipkart is a great business whose growth and potential mirrors that of India as a whole — that’s why we invested in 2018 and why we continue to invest today,” said Judith McKenna, President and CEO of Walmart International, in a statement.</p>\n<p>Flipkart says it has amassed over 350 million registered users across its services &#8212; including fashion e-commerce Myntra &#8212; in the country. &#8220;Flipkart’s logistics and supply chain arm, Ekart, employs more than 100,000 people and makes deliveries to more than 90% of the addressable pin-codes in India, which, coupled with strategic warehouse infrastructure investments, is one of the group’s core strengths. Venturing into the social commerce space, Flipkart recently announced the launch of Shopsy, which will encourage local entrepreneurship,&#8221; the firm said.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a id=\"speakable-summary\">Melissa Wong spent more than a decade working for major retail brands before founding Retail Zipline. That kind of outrageous advantage &#8212; a complete understanding of the industry &#8212; is something that investors struggle to resist in a vertical SaaS company. At least, according to Emergence Capital investor Lotti Siniscalco.</p>\n<p>Wong and Siniscalco joined us on a recent episode of Extra Crunch Live and went into detail on why Emergence was eager to finance Retail Zipline&#8217;s Series A round, walking us through Zipline&#8217;s Series A pitch deck and sharing which slides and bits clinched the deal.</p>\n<p>Extra Crunch Live is a weekly virtual event series meant to help founders build better venture-backed businesses. We sit down with investors and the founders they finance to hear what brought them together, what they saw in each other and how they work together moving forward. We also host the ECL pitch-off, where founders in the audience can pitch their startups to our outstanding speakers.</p>\n<p>Extra Crunch Live is accessible to everyone on a live basis, but the on-demand content is reserved exclusively for Extra Crunch members. You can check out the <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/06/24/check-out-the-expert-speakers-joining-us-on-extra-crunch-live-in-july/\">July slate here</a> and see the full <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/ecl/\">ECL library here</a>.</p>\n<h2>Stand up, stand out</h2>\n<p>During Wong&#8217;s fundraising process, Zipline was also attending a big industry conference. Emergence suggested that they do a virtual pitch meeting while Wong was at the trade show, but Wong pushed back, insisting on an in-person pitch meeting. Not only did she know that she would deliver a better pitch in person, but she didn&#8217;t want to squander the limited amount of time she had at the trade show with potential clients and partners.</p>\n<p>\t<div class=\"article-block block--pullout block--right\">\n\t\t<blockquote>\n\t\t\t&#8220;She pointed to the screen projected behind her to help us stay on the most relevant piece of information. The way she did it really made us stay with her. Like, we couldn&#8217;t break eye contact.&#8221;\t\t\t\t\t</blockquote>\n\t</div>\n\t</p>\n<p>Once the in-person meeting did take place, Wong surprised the Emergence team. For one, she stood up to pitch. Wong explained that her co-founder is a bigger guy, and she&#8217;s a smaller woman, and she feels more confident and comfortable presenting from a standing position.</p>\n<p>&#8220;She was one of the few or maybe the only CEO who ever stood up to pitch the entire team,&#8221; said Siniscalco. &#8220;She pointed to the screen projected behind her to help us stay on the most relevant piece of information. The way she did it really made us stay with her. Like, we couldn&#8217;t break eye contact.&#8221;</p>\n<p>In terms of delivery, Wong had already made an impact. But the content of the deck, and her experience in retail, clinched the deal.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I look for an unfair reason for a founder to be the perfect person to build this product,&#8221; said Siniscalco. &#8220;Wong gave us her background in the first slide, and I knew quickly that she was a credible person in the retail industry. Then, what I look for in a pitch, is customer love.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Siniscalco said the combination of that unfair advantage and intense customer love is highly correlated with a very positive outcome for a company.</p>\n<p>&#8220;When we first started out, I was really insecure <em>because</em> I came from the industry versus coming from a lot of Silicon Valley knowledge,&#8221; said Wong. &#8220;In retrospect, I really underestimated the competitive advantage of coming from the industry. People said it to me, but I didn&#8217;t understand what that resulted in. But it resulted in the numbers in our deck, because I know what customers want, what they want to buy next, how to keep them happy and I was able to be way more capital-efficient.&#8221;</p>\n<h2>The Zipline deck</h2>\n<p>Zipline&#8217;s entire deck (with some minor redactions) is embedded below. You can swipe on through at your leisure, but the real value here (in my humble opinion) is Siniscalco&#8217;s breakdown of how she reacted to the information in the deck.
