Crook","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn20@2020_5/2021/07/12/18-35-19-302_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn20@2020_6/2021/07/12/18-37-22-668_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=bMcrxGj21ZA:Ihxm8EroexA:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn86@2020_1/2021/07/12/18-37-22-322_35f14386e075ceeb.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=bMcrxGj21ZA:Ihxm8EroexA:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn24@2020_2/2021/07/12/18-37-22-328_ecc1d1e5aa6cacc6.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/bMcrxGj21ZA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn7@2020_3/2021/07/12/18-37-22-289_0d6db58c802cf339.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626114919068},{"createdTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","title":"Beyond Pride: The fight against tech’s brogrammer culture","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2175569","description":"<div class=\"article__contributor-byline-wrapper\">\n<div class=\"article__contributor-byline\">\n\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__contributor\">\n\t\t<div class=\"byline__author\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class=\"byline__author-name\">Phil Schraeder</span>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class=\"byline__author-title\" style=\"display: block;\">Contributor</span>\n\t\t</div>\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"contributor__twitter\">\n\t\t\t<a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://twitter.com/philschraeder\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<svg class=\"icon icon--twitter icon--white\" viewBox=\"0 0 20 20\" version=\"1.1\" aria-labelledby=\"title\">\n\t\t<title>Share on Twitter</title>\n\t\t<path d=\"M20,4c-0.7,0.3-1.5,0.6-2.4,0.7c0.9-0.5,1.5-1.4,1.8-2.3c-0.8,0.5-1.7,0.8-2.6,1C16.1,2.5,15,2,13.8,2c-2.3,0-4.1,1.9-4.1,4.2c0,0.3,0,0.7,0.1,1C6.4,7,3.4,5.4,1.4,2.9C1,3.5,0.8,4.1,0.8,4.9c0,1.4,0.7,2.7,1.8,3.5C2,8.4,1.4,8.2,0.8,7.9v0.1c0,2,1.4,3.7,3.3,4.1c-0.4,0.1-0.7,0.2-1.1,0.2c-0.3,0-0.5,0-0.8-0.1c0.5,1.7,2,2.9,3.8,2.9c-1.4,1.1-3.2,2-5.1,2c-0.3,0-0.7,0-1-0.1c1.8,1.2,4,1.7,6.3,1.7c7.5,0,11.7-6.4,11.7-12V6.1C18.8,5.6,19.4,4.8,20,4z\"/>\t</svg>\n\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\n\t\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__bio\">\n\t\t<a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/phil-schraeder-a971855/\">Phil Schraeder</a> is CEO of <a href=\"https://gumgum.com/\">GumGum</a>, the global technology and media company specializing in contextual intelligence.\t</div>\n\t\n\t</div>\n</div><p id=\"speakable-summary\">I was 4 years old when I started playing what I’ve come to think of as “the game.” It was dressing-up time at school, and, as I ran over to a costume box, my teacher grabbed me by the shoulders. Right up in my face, she admonished: “That’s the girls’ box — the boys’ stuff is over there.”</p>\n<p>I was taken aback; I didn’t understand what I’d done wrong. But I remember thinking: “Oh! There are rules to how we live together in the world.” Right then and there, I started conforming to the parameter of the game that so many of us operate by: the game that gives us unwritten codes on what is acceptable and how to behave &#8212; at school, in work or in society at large.</p>\n<p>This game meant I spent years dialing down my “gayness,” even after I came out in my 20s, and the impulse was particularly acute at the early stage of my career. With each new meeting or business deal, I was constantly preempting what parts of me were “OK”’ or what might put people off. Just how much gay was too much?</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>In some ways, then, the endemic “<a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brogrammer\">brogrammer</a>” culture in tech — the industry I call home — is no great surprise to me. When everyone is busy filtering their core identity, sanding down the edges to fit the collective mold, it’s inevitable that minority voices will be pushed out. Follow this picture to its natural conclusion and Silicon Valley — the home of bold disruptors, the armada of innovation — is reduced to a narrow few.</p>\n<p>\t<div class=\"article-block block--pullout block--left\">\n\t\t<blockquote>\n\t\t\tWith Pride Month drawn to a close, it’s my greatest hope that we can use its particular kind of open-minded energy to activate deeper change.\t\t\t\t\t</blockquote>\n\t</div>\n\t</p>\n<p>In many ways, Pride Month and the celebrations we’ve just seen are the antidote to this hegemony. Pride, with its rainbow symbolism, is a cornucopia of all that is free, true and uninhibited. With Pride Month drawn to a close, it’s my greatest hope that we can use its particular kind of open-minded energy to activate deeper change.</p>\n<h2>Show up for your team first</h2>\n<p>I truly love Pride and the meaningful action that goes with it, but it can’t be denied that some brands are venturing into the territory of window dressing. <a href=\"https://realbusiness.co.uk/branding-corporate-performative-activism-pride\">“Performative activism,”</a> whereby companies mobilize the Pride flag for marketing purposes without necessarily making tangible changes in their own backyards, is on the rise. So too are the businesses that pay lip service to Pride from one side of their mouth while covertly supporting politicians behind <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2021/06/20/the-right-way-for-brands-to-approach-pride-month-and-all-year-round.html\">anti-transgender legislation</a> on the other.</p>\n<p>If you are a leader who’s really committed to diversity in the workplace, it stands to reason that you look within to help your own team first. How can you create a culture where employees can be present in the fullness of themselves — regardless of gender, race, sexuality or even incidental things like taste in clothes or music?</p>\n<p>According to a 2019 study by <a href=\"https://medicine.yale.edu/news-article/the-global-closet-is-hugevast-majority-of-worlds-lesbian-gay-bisexual-population-hide-orientation-ysph-study-finds/\">the Yale School of Public Health</a>, an estimated 83% of those who identify as lesbian, gay or bisexual keep their sexuality hidden from all or most of the people in their lives.</p>\n<p>This inhibition is magnified in the workplace, where it is woven into the fabric of myriad discriminatory behaviors that are particularly prominent in tech. Almost <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/lgbtq-employees-tech-companies-witness-discrimination-blind-survey-2019-6?r=US&#38;IR=T\">40% of LGBTQ tech employees</a> polled by anonymous workplace chat app Blind say they&#8217;ve witnessed homophobic discrimination and harassment at work.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.wired.com/story/five-years-tech-diversity-reports-little-progress/\">Annual diversity reports</a> show that Big Tech companies employ far fewer women and underrepresented minorities than other industries, too. This is a sector that routinely labels people from nonmajority culture groups as “diversity hires,” doling out discrimination in everything from pay to promotions &#8212; as reported by thousands of personal experiences shared under the hashtag <a href=\"https://eu.usatoday.com/story/tech/2020/02/10/racial-discrimination-persists-facebook-google-employees-say/4307591002/\">#SiliconValleySoWhite</a>. The same industry is also <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2018/mar/17/sexual-harassment-silicon-valley-emily-chang-brotopia-interview\">hardwired to marginalize women</a>, says Emily Chang, the Bloomberg Technology anchor whose book, “<a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Brotopia-Breaking-Boys-Silicon-Valley/dp/0735213534\">Brotopia</a>,” lifts the lid on Silicon Valley’s culture of machismo.</p>\n<p>These aren’t easy issues to solve, but I believe authenticity has an important part in the solution. It’s about calling time on that game that I used to play. When I finally learned that I could show up as I pleased at work and not worry about how people judge me, the freedom was so sweet I could practically taste it. After years of faking it without fully realizing it &#8212; in a draining, relentless loop &#8212; I was able to be the person and CEO I wanted to be. The more familiar I became with California’s tech scene, and the farther up the ladder I progressed, the more confident I became to be me.</p>\n<p>You shouldn’t have to wait until you run a company for the permission to express your full self, however. As the research shows, the price paid for not doing so reaches far beyond personal freedom alone. Though we’ve made steps with important conversations around diversity in recent years, the world we work in is still, overwhelmingly, one-dimensional. It’s full of people not able or willing to reveal the genuine, hi-def version of who they are.</p>\n<h2>The power of listening and shared vulnerability</h2>\n<p>If we, as tech leaders, are unable to roll our sleeves up and dig deep on the issue of authenticity, we have little hope of chipping away at the <a href=\"https://www.rand.org/blog/2018/05/ending-the-brogrammer-culture-how-to-close-the-gender.html\">“brogrammer” attitude</a> that seems all too pervasive in our industry.</p>\n<p>Not only does this kind of climate engender unsaid <a href=\"https://www.talkspace.com/blog/code-switching-what-is/\">fear, fatigue and anxiety</a>, it also affects the bottom line. Research is clear on the fact that happy employees are <a href=\"https://www.ox.ac.uk/news/2019-10-24-happy-workers-are-13-more-productive\">more productive</a>, while companies with more diverse management teams have greater <a href=\"https://www.weforum.org/agenda/2019/04/business-case-for-diversity-in-the-workplace/\">profitability, creativity and problem-solving abilities</a>. Having the freedom to be your authentic self at work is a conduit to success and fulfillment.</p>\n<p>So, how can tech CEOs and management get to this place? In my mind, a dual-sided approach is called for. First, efforts to harness authentic expression have to be enacted as policies. Leaders must give their teams direct responsibility for helping employees to bring their full selves to work. Help make your people accountable for an inside effort allowing all voices in your organization to be heard.</p>\n<p>In GumGum’s case, this includes the formation of a STRIDE (Seeking Talent Representation Inclusion Diversity &#38; Equity) Council. Made up of employees from all divisions, locations and levels of seniority across the company, council members make tangible recommendations to improve diversity and inclusivity in the company as part of their paid daily roles.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.hcamag.com/ca/specialization/diversity-inclusion/five-myths-on-unconscious-bias-and-how-to-tackle-the-issue/259328\">Unconscious bias training</a> is also vital for empowering authentic expression in the workplace. If I walked down the street in glitter shorts and a crop top, everyone around me would have some kind of reaction to my chosen outfit — regardless of whether they’d admit it. Building awareness of subconscious judgments like this is the first step to reining them in, and creates understanding of how bias inevitably impacts decision-making at work.</p>\n<p>Second, the quest for business authenticity lies with CEOs and senior management and their ability to lead by example. I think today&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/business-54374824\">cancel culture</a> has made leaders hypersensitive about the need to keep it together, to toe the line with their behavior, to be professional and not make mistakes.</p>\n<p>Professionalism has its time and a place, of course, but I’ve always made it a point to be as open as possible as a CEO &#8212; to shine a light over every element of my personality, even the aspects that other people may judge or find less desirable. My determination to do this comes directly from the hidden identity that I used to struggle with. The fear I felt over being gay is now my fuel to showing my true self. By doing so, I aim to give those around me permission to do the same.</p>\n<p>No one really wants their tech company to breed a bro culture where only one type of person can thrive. But it’s not enough to simply say that. You have to start by <em>showing</em> that it&#8217;s OK to be different, to turn up in every shade of gray. I have a penchant for flamboyant fashion, for example, so I don’t think twice about attending a Zoom meeting in a baby blue fedora. That’s just how I express myself as a CEO.</p>\n<p>Showing up like this involves an element of fear, and I think it’s important to be open about that, too. As CEOs, we should share our vulnerabilities, our struggles with identity, the secret parts of ourselves that we’re tempted to keep masked away. This includes owning up to failures &#8212; CEOs are only human, and that humanity should be put on a pedestal if authenticity is the goal.</p>\n<p>People need to feel that their vulnerabilities are heard without judgment. Whether they&#8217;re in an interview or taking on a new project, one of my favorite questions to ask employees is simply, “What are you afraid of?”</p>\n<p>We all have fears, and by answering that question, you get to access someone’s vulnerable side. They might be scared of failing, making the wrong decision or upsetting the apple cart in some way. Tapping into that emotion is a great way of giving people permission to be their full selves.</p>\n<h2>A turning point for tech</h2>\n<p>Pride Month is part of a wider narrative around acceptance and freedom of being. Companies that jump on the rainbow bandwagon <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2021/06/20/the-right-way-for-brands-to-approach-pride-month-and-all-year-round.html\">without fully living those values</a> aren’t only hypocritical — they’re also doing themselves a disservice. Pride isn’t a revenue opportunity, and even if it was, those brands that attach messaging to it without substance are missing a trick.</p>\n<p>Beneath the LGBTQ+ Pride gift wrap lies a thousand work environments in urgent need of the values that the Pride movement espouses. Making those values a living, breathing part of everyday work life is no mean feat. But allowing people to untether from who they “should&#8221; be at work is a vital starting point for a change that is long overdue.</p>\n<p>I know the shame of hiding my true self away, which is why I make every effort for others to avoid that experience. Nowadays, I show up at work as more myself than I’d ever dared in my younger years. In this one small act, I challenge my co-workers to follow suit. It’s only when, together, we embark on that exploration of what authenticity in business looks like that the endless game-playing can stop — and the real work gets underway.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"rXqe5RUxvu\"><p><a space (or the vicinity of space)</a> in a PR-suffused event over the weekend. It was all rather twee, packed with maudlin riffs about childhood dreams and riddled with hero worship. And the stream kept stuttering while some of the planned vehicle-to-Earth communications failed.</p> \n<hr /> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><b><i>The Exchange is <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/09/startups-have-never-had-it-so-good/\">continuing its look into Q2 venture capital results this week</a>. Use subject line “hot dang look at all this money.” Thanks! — <a href=\"http://twitter.com/alex\">Alex</a> and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/abracarioca\">Anna</a></i></b></p> \n<hr /> \n<p>But the launch accomplished what it set out to do: A few folks made it to into zero gravity after launching their rocket-powered space plane from a larger aircraft, flipping it around at the top of its arc so that its passengers could get a good view of our home while floating. Then it came back to the surface and, we’re sure, much champagne was consumed.</p> \n<p>In the aftermath of the event, lots of folks are pissed. Complaints have rolled in, dissing the event and generally mocking the expense involved when there are other issues to manage. A sampling follows. Note that these are merely illustrative examples of a general vibe. I have precisely zero beef with anyone in the following tweets or articles:</p> \n<div class=\"embed breakout\"> \n <blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\"> \n  <p Tribune</a>:</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://tribunemag.co.uk/2021/07/leave-the-billionaires-in-space\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout aligncenter size-full wp-image-2175992\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Screen-Shot-2021-07-12-at-9.08.21-AM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"425\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Screen-Shot-2021-07-12-at-9.08.21-AM.png 1146w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Screen-Shot-2021-07-12-at-9.08.21-AM.png?resize=768,319 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Screen-Shot-2021-07-12-at-9.08.21-AM.png?resize=680,282 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Screen-Shot-2021-07-12-at-9.08.21-AM.png?resize=50,21 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a></p> \n<p>I disagree.</p> \n<p>Sure, it’s maddening that Jeff Bezos’ new yacht will <a href=\"https://www.msn.com/en-us/news/politics/jeff-bezos-roasted-for-buying-yacht-so-big-it-comes-with-smaller-support-yacht/ar-BB1gEIEK\">require a second boat</a> so that he can have a mobile heliport on the go — his new boat has sails, so you can’t chopper to it — while the company that built his fortune <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2021/06/15/us/amazon-workers.html?action=click&amp;amp;module=Top%20Stories&amp;amp;pgtype=Homepage\">churns through workers with abandon</a>&nbsp;and <a href=\"https://www.cbsnews.com/news/amazon-drivers-peeing-in-bottles-union-vote-worker-complaints/\">squeezes its drivers</a> so much that they have to piss in bottles due to scheduling constraints.</p> \n<p>And, yes, Branson is annoying quite a lot of the time. He also owns an island and likes himself too much.\n <div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"></div>\n <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n  <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=lHfP2fAKpfw:4QpDvuIAcuk:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\" /></a> \n  <a /></a> \n </div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/lHfP2fAKpfw\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\" /></p>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 12 Jul 2021 14:21:33 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.0.1/72x72/2728.png","linkMd5":"ac636ab4bc51dc8d0dbe3f8095ca952e","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn16@2020_5/2021/07/12/18-35-19-357_1409635f53f81b02.webp","destWidth":72,"destHeight":72,"sourceBytes":752,"destBytes":1494,"author":"Alex Wilhelm","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.0.1/72x72/2728.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn16@2020_5/2021/07/12/18-35-19-357_1409635f53f81b02.webp","https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.0.1/72x72/262e.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn94@2020_6/2021/07/12/18-37-22-313_e1679176a69a835e.webp","https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.0.1/72x72/1f499.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn77@2020_1/2021/07/12/18-37-22-665_09a0b4d40837f560.webp","https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Screen-Shot-2021-07-12-at-9.08.21-AM.png":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn20@2020_5/2021/07/12/18-35-19-302_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn20@2020_6/2021/07/12/18-37-22-668_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=lHfP2fAKpfw:4QpDvuIAcuk:-BTjWOF_DHI":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=lHfP2fAKpfw:4QpDvuIAcuk:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn54@2020_1/2021/07/12/18-37-22-850_6f3fb30d82819f06.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/lHfP2fAKpfw":null},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626114919067},{"createdTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","title":"Virgin Galactic and Richard Branson celebrate launch of first passengers into space","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2175878","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Virgin Galactic has successfully taken its first passengers to space, including its billionaire founder Richard Branson. The event, at Spaceport America in New Mexico, was a field day for press and employees, complete with an early-morning Khalid set and hero walk by Branson and the crew.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Just imagine a world where people of all ages, all backgrounds, from anywhere, of any gender, of any ethnicity, have equal access to space,&#8221; Branson said on returning. &#8220;Welcome to the dawn of a new space age!&#8221;</p>\n<p>The remark is a bit premature, of course — that world is still some distance off, but it&#8217;s true that this flight marks a historic moment in the nascent space tourism industry. At present, leisurenauts are still an elite class, but the events of the day suggest we&#8217;re closer than ever to seeing that change.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>After an incredibly early start to the day (shuttles to the Spaceport left at 2:45 AM from nearby Las Cruces), the festivities began in true space launch style with a delay. A thunderstorm overnight prevented the team from rolling out the spacecraft, which believe it or not can&#8217;t get wet. At the speeds and temperatures involved nothing can be left to chance — like ice forming from water in or on the chassis.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2175898\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/P1010053.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2175898\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2175898\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/P1010053.jpg\" alt=\"Press set up before dawn at Spaceport America.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"654\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/P1010053.jpg 2500w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/P1010053.jpg?resize=150,96 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/P1010053.jpg?resize=300,192 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/P1010053.jpg?resize=768,490 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/P1010053.jpg?resize=680,434 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/P1010053.jpg?resize=1536,981 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/P1010053.jpg?resize=2048,1307 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/P1010053.jpg?resize=50,32 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2175898\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Devin Coldewey / TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p>Soon the sun rose and crowds arrived: VIPs, employees, a bunch of local students, and Branson&#8217;s own guest list (reportedly numbering around 150). <a href=\"https://twitter.com/richardbranson/status/1414199651037716485\">Elon Musk showed up as well</a>, presumably to congratulate his fellow spaceman personally, billionaire to billionaire.</p>\n<p>At 8:30 local time the engines started on VMS Eve, the &#8220;mothership&#8221; carrying VSS Unity, the rocket-powered spaceplane that Branson, along with Virgin Galactic&#8217;s Beth Moses (her second flight), Sirisha Bandla, and Colin Bennett, would ride to the edge of space.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2175906\" style=\"width: 1415px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/eve-takeoff.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2175906\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2175906 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/eve-takeoff.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1405\" height=\"787\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/eve-takeoff.jpg 1405w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/eve-takeoff.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/eve-takeoff.jpg?resize=300,168 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/eve-takeoff.jpg?resize=768,430 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/eve-takeoff.jpg?resize=680,381 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/eve-takeoff.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1405px) 100vw, 1405px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2175906\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">VMS Eve takes off. <strong>Image Credits:</strong> Virgin Galactic</p></div></p>\n<p>Eve was wheels up at 8:40, commencing a wait on the ground while it climbed to about 36,000 feet. Unity detached and began its rocket-powered climb at about 9:24, reaching Mach 3 and after two minutes reached its peak altitude of about 282,000 feet — about 53 miles, as planned.</p>\n<p>The crew and passengers enjoyed a minute or two of microgravity, which they seem to have employed gainfully:</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2175909\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Unity-3_6.00_41_15_01.Still002.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2175909\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2175909\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Unity-3_6.00_41_15_01.Still002.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Unity-3_6.00_41_15_01.Still002.jpg 1920w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Unity-3_6.00_41_15_01.Still002.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Unity-3_6.00_41_15_01.Still002.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Unity-3_6.00_41_15_01.Still002.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Unity-3_6.00_41_15_01.Still002.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Unity-3_6.00_41_15_01.Still002.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Unity-3_6.00_41_15_01.Still002.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2175909\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Virgin Galactic</p></div></p>\n<p>A planned mid-air speech by Branson proved impossible as the signal cut in and out, but the craft itself proved more reliable, touching down at 9:38.</p>\n<p>In a celebratory stage appearance (following a brief Khalid concert) Branson expanded on the ideas cut short in transmission, beginning with: &#8220;It&#8217;s hot, I&#8217;m sorry,&#8221; but quickly moving on to more inspiring words. &#8220;I have dreamt about this moment since I was a child, but nothing could have prepared me for the view of Earth from space. We are at the vanguard of a new space age.&#8221;</p>\n<p>At a press conference following shortly after, Branson fielded questions from elementary schoolers, and the crew described the view from space and whether they saw any planets. (No, just an alien that the pilot shook off during descent, Branson said. At least one kid I saw believed him.)</p>\n<h2>A long road to space</h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2086560\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Virgin_Galactic_Pilots_on_their_way_to_the_Virgin_Galactic_Spaceflight_System.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2086560\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2086560\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Virgin_Galactic_Pilots_on_their_way_to_the_Virgin_Galactic_Spaceflight_System.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Virgin_Galactic_Pilots_on_their_way_to_the_Virgin_Galactic_Spaceflight_System.jpg 2560w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Virgin_Galactic_Pilots_on_their_way_to_the_Virgin_Galactic_Spaceflight_System.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Virgin_Galactic_Pilots_on_their_way_to_the_Virgin_Galactic_Spaceflight_System.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Virgin_Galactic_Pilots_on_their_way_to_the_Virgin_Galactic_Spaceflight_System.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Virgin_Galactic_Pilots_on_their_way_to_the_Virgin_Galactic_Spaceflight_System.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Virgin_Galactic_Pilots_on_their_way_to_the_Virgin_Galactic_Spaceflight_System.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Virgin_Galactic_Pilots_on_their_way_to_the_Virgin_Galactic_Spaceflight_System.jpg?resize=2048,1366 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Virgin_Galactic_Pilots_on_their_way_to_the_Virgin_Galactic_Spaceflight_System.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2086560\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Virgin Galactic Pilots on their way to the Virgin Galactic Spaceflight System. <strong>Image Credits: </strong>Virgin Galactic</p></div></p>\n<p>It&#8217;s a triumph long in the making for Virgin Galactic and Branson. The company was ahead of the curve in its space tourism ambitions, but in 2014 a test flight <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2014/10/31/virgin-galactics-spaceshiptwo-has-crashed/\">ended in a horrific crash</a> and the death of one of the pilots.</p>\n<p>Virgin&#8217;s engineers and leaders worked through it, however, and built a stronger, better spacecraft which was christened Unity by Stephen Hawking, who was then still living — and, not surprisingly, hoping to hitch a ride someday.</p>\n<p>Pilots flew test flight after test flight over the years, slowly ratcheting up the power and finally, in 2018, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/12/13/virgin-galactic-touches-the-edge-of-space-with-mach-2-9-test-flight-of-spaceshiptwo/\">touching the edge of space</a>. On that note there is some slight controversy in that the exact altitude where the atmosphere gives way to space isn&#8217;t completely agreed upon. Some authorities place the Kármán line, as the imaginary boundary is called, at 100 kilometers above sea level, others at 50 miles, or about 80 kilometers.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2175922\" style=\"width: 1930px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/virgin-galactic-u22-space.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2175922\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2175922 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/virgin-galactic-u22-space.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1920\" height=\"1080\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/virgin-galactic-u22-space.jpg 1920w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/virgin-galactic-u22-space.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/virgin-galactic-u22-space.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/virgin-galactic-u22-space.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/virgin-galactic-u22-space.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/virgin-galactic-u22-space.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/virgin-galactic-u22-space.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1920px) 100vw, 1920px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2175922\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Unity 22 spreads its &#8220;feathers&#8221; during descent. <strong>Image Credits:</strong> Virgin Galactic</p></div></p>\n<p>Virgin uses the lower estimate, while its arch rival, Jeff Bezos&#8217;s Blue Origin, uses the higher. This led Bezos to throw shade on Virgin&#8217;s flights, saying he didn&#8217;t want his customers to have an &#8220;asterisk&#8221; on their trip to space. When I asked about this before, a Virgin representative said they use the same standard that NASA and the U.S. Air Force does: pilots are given their &#8220;astronaut wings&#8221; if they pass the 50-mile mark.</p>\n<p>Kármán quibbles aside, the race to send passengers to space has been heating up lately, and Bezos recently announced that he would be flying aboard the first crewed launch of Blue Origin&#8217;s New Shepard rocket on July 22 — with his brother, a mystery passenger who has paid $28M for the privilege, and Wally Funk, among the first women trained to be astronauts in 1961 but who never made it to space.</p>\n<p>But Branson rained on his parade by announcing shortly afterward that he would fly aboard Virgin&#8217;s first passenger launch to space (crew and pilots have been up several times) about a week earlier.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"YOtB7mXPck\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/01/branson-aims-to-beat-bezos-to-orbit-in-final-stretch-of-billionaire-space-race/\">Branson aims to beat Bezos to orbit in final stretch of billionaire space race</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Branson aims to beat Bezos to orbit in final stretch of billionaire space race&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/01/branson-aims-to-beat-bezos-to-orbit-in-final-stretch-of-billionaire-space-race/embed/#?secret=YOtB7mXPck\" data-secret=\"YOtB7mXPck\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>While Branson has good-naturedly denied any competition between himself and Bezos (&#8220;We wish Jeff the absolute best,&#8221; he said, adding that Bezos sent over a message of goodwill before the flight) it&#8217;s hard to believe that&#8217;s completely true. Though neither man has anything to prove at this point, there must surely be some satisfaction in Branson&#8217;s not merely going to space (a lifelong dream, as he tells it) but doing so before his upstart rival. However much he denies it, the narrative is too tempting to quash completely.</p>\n<p>The direction forward for Virgin Galactic now is, clearly, towards paying customers, of which there are plenty lined up. Of course, they all have a quarter of a million dollars to spare, but you might not, and for you Branson has a special offer. <a href=\"https://www.omaze.com/products/virgin-galactic-2021\">They&#8217;ve partnered with Omaze</a>, and donations to the chosen charity will enter you into a raffle of sorts, with the winner receiving two tickets on an upcoming Virgin Galactic flight. &#8220;And with my Willy Wonka hat on, a guided tour of Spaceport America, given by yours truly,&#8221; Branson added.</p>\n<p>Branson expressed hope that this would become an ongoing thing as long as donations continue, so perhaps this is the answer to the question of how they hope to, as he so frequently promises, make space available to <em>everyone</em>.</p>\n<p>You can watch the whole day unfold as it happened in Virgin Galactic&#8217;s archived livestream below:</p>\n<p><iframe class=\"youtube-player\" width=\"640\" 021-07-13 02:35:19","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","title":"Dovetail, the venture studio that has worked with startups like Afterpay, is raising a new fund","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2175945","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><div id=\"attachment_2175946\" style=\"width: 4042px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Ash-and-Nick.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2175946\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2175946 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Ash-and-Nick.jpg\" alt=\"A photo of Dovetail co-founders Ash Fogelberg and Nick Frandsen\" width=\"4032\" height=\"3024\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Ash-and-Nick.jpg 4032w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Ash-and-Nick.jpg?resize=150,113 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Ash-and-Nick.jpg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Ash-and-Nick.jpg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Ash-and-Nick.jpg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Ash-and-Nick.jpg?resize=1536,1152 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Ash-and-Nick.jpg?resize=2048,1536 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Ash-and-Nick.jpg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 4032px) 100vw, 4032px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2175946\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Dovetail co-founders Ash Fogelberg and Nick Frandsen</p></div></p>\n<p>Based in Sydney and Auckland, <a href=\"https://dovetailstudios.com/\">Dovetail</a> is a full-service venture studio that works closely with founders who have a great idea, but may lack technical backgrounds. Dovetail helps them build companies from the ground up, preparing them for growth and more funding. Founded in 2014, Dovetail’s success stories include <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/afterpay/\">Afterpay</a>, the Melbourne-headquartered unicorn that is one of the highest-profile players in the buy now, play later space, along with Klarna and Affirm.</p>\n<p>“People can think of us as the technical co-founder, responsible for driving and executing product strategy, design and the development of scalable products,” Dovetail co-founder Nick Frandsen told TechCrunch.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Dovetail is currently raising a $10 million AUD (about $7.5 million USD) fund that will be used for seed, Series A and Series B rounds in 15 of the most promising companies that have gone through its venture studio program. As an investor, Dovetail has written check sizes ranging from $150,000 to $1 million AUD.</p>\n<p>One of Dovetail’s goals is prepare startups to seek funding from other VCs; firms that have invested in Dovetail’s portfolio companies include Blackbird, Qantas and Wavemaker.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Z5SgEShOR6\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/06/04/as-buy-now-pay-later-startups-keep-raising-capital-a-dive-into-klarna-afterpay-and-affirms-earnings/\">As buy now, pay later startups keep raising capital, a dive into Klarna, Afterpay and Affirm&#8217;s earnings</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;As buy now, pay later startups keep raising capital, a dive into Klarna, Afterpay and Affirm&#8217;s earnings&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/06/04/as-buy-now-pay-later-startups-keep-raising-capital-a-dive-into-klarna-afterpay-and-affirms-earnings/embed/#?secret=Z5SgEShOR6\" data-secret=\"Z5SgEShOR6\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>“By the time we need to make an investment decision, we would have worked collaboratively on a day-to-day basis with them for at least three months prior to a seed round and 12 months for a Series A. This means we’re essentially investing with the informational edge of a co-founder,” said Frandsen. “Another trait that makes Dovetail unique is that we share our ownership in our portfolio companies with the entire team. This further drives unity, dedication and a desire to succeed from our team.”</p>\n<p>Dovetail began working with Afterpay in 2017, when the company had less than 40 employees. Frandsen said Afterpay’s founders, Nick Molnar and Anthony Eisen, were looking for a digital product development partner to build and scale their mobile and web apps. While both had deep experience in financial services, they came from non-technical backgrounds. That’s where Dovetail came into play, building out Afterpay’s tech platforms and helping launch its consumer-facing products.</p>\n<p>Some other notable startups that have gone through its venture studio program are resource planning SaaS platform <a href=\"https://www.runn.io/\">Runn</a>; one-click invoicing tool <a href=\"https://www.withmarmalade.com.au/\">Marmalade</a>; <a href=\"https://providerchoice.com.au/\">Provider Choice</a>, a management platform for providers in Australia’s National Disability Insurance Scheme; <a href=\"https://www.landmarksid.com/\">Landmarks ID</a>, a privacy-compliant mobile location intelligence platform for marketers; and <a href=\"https://www.fluenccy.com/\">Fluenccy</a>, a service that helps importers and exporters save money on foreign exchange.</p>\n<p>Before they started Dovetail, Frandsen and co-founder Ash Fogelberg’s startup, ticketing and payments platform 1-Night, was acquired by TicketDirect in 2013.</p>\n<p>Dovetail’s venture studio is sector-agnostic (though it has strong experience in fintech, SaaS and marketplaces), and works with startups that may not have a product yet, but have founders who “are ambitious, commercially-savvy and bring industry expertise from the field in which they are trying to solve a problem,” said Frandsen.</p>\n<p>When deciding what founders to work with, Dovetail considers at the viability and growth potential of their idea.This includes looking at how well-suited founders are to the issue, if there is enough market potential for the startup to grow into a large company and how much competition there is.</p>\n<p>Dovetail has a product agency that serves mostly U.S. companies, but its venture studio is currently focused on Australasian startups, with plans to expand into North America in the future.</p>\n<p>“We are actively seeking industries that are large yet underappreciated by the startup community,” Frandsen said. “We’re looking for ideas. that require hard-earned industry experience and can’t easily be replicated by teams of young aspiring entrepreneurs.”</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote cross-sells a small sachet of insurance and loans as well as provides them with American Express-powered credit cards, is targeting a valuation of about $1 billion in the IPO, according to two people 02:35:19","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","title":"Elon Musk defends Tesla’s $2.6B acquisition of SolarCity in Delaware court","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2176148","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Elon Musk is testifying Monday morning in a lawsuit over Tesla’s 2016 acquisition of SolarCity, a $2.6 billion transaction that a group of shareholders allege was a “bailout” of the failing solar company. The shareholders are seeking repayment to Tesla of the cost to purchase SolarCity.</p>\n<p>The suit, filed in the Delaware District Court in 2017, alleges that SolarCity was near bankruptcy at the time of the acquisition. Musk, who was the ailing company’s chairman of the board of directors and its largest stockholder, directly benefited from the transaction, as did some of his friends and family, the lawsuit alleges. SolarCity’s founders, Lyndon and Peter Rive, are Musk’s cousins.</p>\n<p>SolarCity “had consistently failed to turn a profit, had mounting debt, and was burning through cash at an unsustainable rate,” the plaintiffs say. The suit goes on to note that the company had accumulated over $3 billion in debt in its 10-year history, nearly half of which was due for repayment before the end of 2017. The purchase by Tesla was approved by vote by 85% of shareholders.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Attorneys for Musk say that the acquisition was part of the CEO’s longer-term vision to transform Tesla into a transportation and energy company. In a blog post titled “<a href=\"https://www.tesla.com/blog/master-plan-part-deux\">Master Plan, Part Deux</a>,” published to Tesla’s website around the time of the deal’s closing, Musk says that combining SolarCity and the electric vehicle startup was key to realizing his vision of combining Powerwall (Tesla’s home and industry battery storage product) and solar roof panels.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1463267\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1463267\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-1463267\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/tesla-kauai-14.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"682\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/tesla-kauai-14.jpg 2000w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/tesla-kauai-14.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/tesla-kauai-14.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/tesla-kauai-14.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/tesla-kauai-14.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/tesla-kauai-14.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/tesla-kauai-14.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-1463267\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">A Model X stood ready for inspection by attendees at the Kauai solar storage facility launch. Tesla acquired SolarCity in November 2016. <strong>Image Credits:</strong> Darrell Etherington</p></div></p>\n<p>In his testimony Monday, Musk said Tesla was forced to shift focus away from its solar business to meet production deadlines for the Model 3 sedan, The Washington Post’s Will Oremus <a href=\"https://twitter.com/WillOremus/status/1414595938186932227\">tweeted</a> from outside the courtroom. USA Today reporter Isabel Hughes, also at the courtroom, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/izzihughes_/status/1414598289475911682\">tweeted</a> that Musk blamed the pandemic for poor performance of the company’s solar division. He was being questioned by attorney for the plaintiffs Randall Baron, whom Musk called “a shameful person” at a 2019 deposition.</p>\n<p>Musk’s lawyers say that he recused himself from board discussions and negotiations relating to the acquisition &#8212; but the plaintiffs maintain that the recusal was “superficial.” A primary question for the court will be whether Musk exerted undue influence over the transaction, and whether he and other board members concealed information relating to the transaction from shareholders.</p>\n<p>The other board members named in the suit &#8212; Robyn Denholm, Ira Ehrenpreis, Antonio Gracias, Kimbal Musk and Stephen Jurvetson &#8212; settled for $60 million last year, plus $16.8 million in legal fees and expenses, paid for by insurance. The trial, with Musk as the sole defendant, was postponed a year due to the coronavirus pandemic.</p>\n<p>The trial is expected to last 10 business days. The Delaware Court of Chancery, where the suit is being heard, does not have a jury; instead, the case will be heard by judge Vice-Chancellor Joseph Slights III. Even if Slights finds that the deal was improper, he could order Musk to pay far less than the $2.6 billion that Tesla paid for SolarCity at the time.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"2XW39Pjn2y\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/12/eat-the-rich-but-let-them-build-rockets-in-the-meantime/\">Eat the rich, but let them build rockets in the meantime</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Eat the rich, but let them build rockets in the id=\"speakable-summary\">Bioengineering may soon provide compelling, low-carbon alternatives in industries where even the best methods produce significant emissions. Utilizing natural and engineered biological process has led to low-carbon textiles from Algiknit, cell-cultured premium meats from Orbillion, and fuels captured from waste emissions via LanzaTech — and leaders from those companies will be joining us on stage <a href=\"https://hopin.com/events/extreme-tech-challenge-global-finals-presented-by-techcrunch?ref=aa110dd2add8\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">for the Extreme Tech Challenge Global Finals on July 22</a>.</p>\n<p>We&#8217;re co-hosting the event, with panels like this one all day and a pitch-off that will feature a number of innovative startups with a sustainability angle.</p>\n<p>I&#8217;ll be moderating a panel on using bioengineering to create change directly in industries with large carbon footprints: textiles, meat production, and manufacturing.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.algiknit.com/\">Algiknit</a> is a startup that is sourcing raw material for fabric from kelp, which is an eco-friendly alternative to textile crop monocultures and artificial materials like acrylic. CEO Aaron Nesser will speak to the challenge of breaking into this established industry and overcoming preconceived notions of what an algae-derived fabric might be like (spoiler: it&#8217;s like any other fabric).</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.orbillion.com/\">Orbillion Bio</a> is one of the new crop of alternative protein companies offering cell-cultured meats (just don&#8217;t call them &#8220;lab&#8221; or &#8220;vat&#8221; grown) to offset the incredibly wasteful livestock industry. But it&#8217;s more than just growing a steak — there are regulatory and market barriers aplenty that CEO Patricia Bubner can speak to as well as the technical challenge.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.lanzatech.com/\">LanzaTech</a> works with factories to capture emissions as they&#8217;re emitted, collecting the useful particles that would otherwise clutter the atmosphere and repurposing them in the form of premium fuels. This is a delicate and complex process that needs to be a partnership, not just a retrofitting operation, so CEO Jennifer Holmgren will speak to their approach convincing the industry to work with them at the ground floor.</p>\n<p>It should be a very interesting conversation, so tune in on July 22 to hear these and other industry leaders focused on sustainability discuss how innovation at the startup level can contribute to the fight against climate change. <a href=\"https://hopin.com/events/extreme-tech-challenge-global-finals-presented-by-techcrunch?ref=aa110dd2add8\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Plus it&#8217;s free!</a></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=uzJ2Cx3mNng:YyLtQ6yQ7ns:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/uzJ2Cx3mNng\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 12 Jul 2021 16:02:47 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI","linkMd5":"71998055db2f96eb2849b8218ce18d34","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn20@2020_5/2021/07/12/18-35-19-302_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","destWidth":59,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":990,"destBytes":324,"author":"Devin Coldewey","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn20@2020_5/2021/07/12/18-35-19-302_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn20@2020_6/2021/07/12/18-37-22-668_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=uzJ2Cx3mNng:YyLtQ6yQ7ns:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn18@2020_1/2021/07/12/18-37-22-325_ef851b32c55fa740.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=uzJ2Cx3mNng:YyLtQ6yQ7ns:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn62@2020_6/2021/07/12/18-37-22-622_3e6d6ee28197882b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/uzJ2Cx3mNng":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn75@2020_4/2021/07/12/18-37-22-319_84394538293492fc.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626114919067},{"createdTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","title":"Elevate Brands banks $250M to roll up third-party merchants selling on Amazon’s marketplace","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2175995","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The Amazon roll-up play &#8212; where one company creates economies of scale by buying up and consolidating multiple smaller third-party merchants that sell their goods via Amazon&#8217;s marketplace &#8212; continues to be a strong e-commerce trend, and in the latest development, one of the hopefuls in this space is announcing a major injection of capital to fuel its own place in the field.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.elevatebrands.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Elevate Brands</a>, a New York- and Austin-based startup that acquires and runs third-party Amazon merchants, has picked up $250 million in funding, money that it will be using both to continue investing in its technology, as well as to buy up more small businesses.</p>\n<p>Elevate is already profitable, with 25 brands currently in its stable, many of which also have come to Elevate with patents for their products, CEO and founder Ryan Gnesin told TechCrunch. The plan will be to continue to enhance the systems it has in place for evaluating potential M&#38;A and analyzing the landscape overall &#8212; today its algorithms use some 100 million data points, it says, to find suitable acquisition targets &#8212; and to continue building out other organizational efficiencies.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Elevate&#8217;s funding is coming as a mix of debt and equity &#8212; quite standard for these e-commerce businesses that are raising huge rounds to go after the roll-up opportunity &#8212; with backers including a number of individuals and investors with track records in fintech and e-commerce. They include FJ Labs, Novel TMT, Adam Jacobs (who founded The Iconic in Australia), the founders of buy now, pay later business QuadPay, Intermix (acquired by Gap) founder Khajak Keledjian, Ron Suber (of YieldStreet and MoneyLion) and more. No valuation is being disclosed.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.feedbackexpress.com/amazon-1029528-new-sellers-year-plus-stats/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">estimated</a> there are some 5 million third-party sellers on Amazon today, with some 1 million sellers joining the platform in 2020 alone. Thrasio &#8212; one of Elevated&#8217;s larger consolidator-competitors &#8212; believes that around 50,000 of them are making $1 million or more annually in sales. Elevate estimates that the Amazon marketplace, currently valued at $300 billion, will double in the next five years.</p>\n<p>Unsurprisingly, all that has led to a number of companies like Elevated racking up hundreds of millions of dollars in debt and equity to consolidate the most promising of these businesses. Their rationale: The founders and management of these third-party sellers may lack the appetite to stay with their businesses for the longer-term, or they may lack the capital to scale to the next level; so consolidating these businesses to leverage investments in technology for better market analytics, marketing, manufacturing and supply chains is the logical solution.</p>\n<p>Given the size of the market opportunity, that&#8217;s led to a lot of investment. Thrasio has raised <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/01/thrasio-raises-100m-for-its-amazon-roll-up-play-appoints-retail-cfo-heavyweight-for-its-next-steps/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">nearly $2 billion</a> &#8212; in both debt and equity &#8212; for its efforts; Heyday recently <a href=\"https://heyday.co/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">raised $70 million</a> from General Catalyst; The Razor Group in Berlin <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/05/04/berlins-razor-group-raises-400m-to-buy-and-scale-amazon-marketplace-merchants/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">raised $400 million</a>. Others with huge war chests include <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/02/09/target-global-leads-150m-round-for-amazon-marketplace-consolidator-branded/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Branded</a>; <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/10/heroes/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Heroes</a>; <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/19/sellerx-raises-118m-to-buy-up-and-grow-amazon-marketplace-businesses/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">SellerX</a>; <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/20/perch-raises-123-5m-to-grow-its-stable-of-d2c-brands-that-sell-on-amazon/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Perch</a>; <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/01/28/berlin-brands-group-commits-302m-to-acquire-d2c-and-amazon-merchants/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Berlin Brands Group</a> (<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/13/berlin-brands-group-raises-240m-to-buy-and-scale-up-third-party-amazon-marketplace-brands/\">X2</a>); <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/26/benitago-group-funding/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Benitago</a>; Latin America’s <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/02/16/valoreo-raises-50m-to-roll-up-latam-e-commerce-brands/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Valoreo</a> and emerging groups out of Asia including <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/05/05/founded-by-former-carousell-ovo-and-fave-execs-rainforest-raises-36m-to-aggregate-asia-pacific-amazon-marketplace-sellers/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Rainforest</a> and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/05/05/una-brands-launches-with-40m-to-acquire-brands-on-multiple-asia-pacific-e-commerce-platforms/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Una Brands</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"SKEnADSIcL\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/02/16/valoreo-raises-50m-to-roll-up-latam-e-commerce-brands/\">Valoreo closes on $50M to roll up LatAm e-commerce brands</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Valoreo closes on $50M to roll up LatAm e-commerce brands&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/02/16/valoreo-raises-50m-to-roll-up-latam-e-commerce-brands/embed/#?secret=SKEnADSIcL\" data-secret=\"SKEnADSIcL\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Elevate&#8217;s pitch to the market is that it&#8217;s a little different from the rest of the roll-up pack, in that it started out as one of the millions of third-party sellers itself.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We started selling at the end of 2016, testing the waters by selling a few private label products,&#8221; Ryan Gnesin, the CEO and founder of Elevated, told TechCrunch in an interview. That gave the company an early look at how to handle supply chains in manufacturing, and to think about how to differentiate its products from similar ones that are sold alongside them on Amazon. <span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">By 2017, Elevate was managing some 8,000 SKUs under that model. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">That shifted in 2018 to a wholesale model, he said, reselling established brands on Amazon. It ran into trouble multiple times in that period, with Amazon shutting it down three times under suspicion of running counterfeit activities. </span></p>\n<p>&#8220;We got caught up in an algorithm because we were scaling so quickly,&#8221; he said. &#8220;They assumed we were doing something wrong.&#8221; All of that helped Elevate learn how to navigate the waters more adeptly, with the first shut down taking three months to fix, but the second only one month, and the third a mere 24 hours. Eventually, in 2019, the company decided to take what it had learned and apply it to a wider range of brands, which it would pick up by way of acquisition.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We began as third-party merchants and so we truly relate to them,&#8221; he said. &#8220;We didn’t just wake up and start buying Amazon businesses. This is what we are in our core, operators first. Anyone can buy a business, but the ones who can grow them are the most successful. That is our long-term view.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Companies that become the target of roll-up acquirers are an interesting lot. As Gnesin describes it, in many cases the businesses Elevate talks to were built as side-hustles, and so when they take off, the founders are just as happy to pass them on to someone else for a decent exit than they are to stay the course. This is one reason why some of the acquisitions end up staying confidential, he said. Another is that the sellers are simply getting on, looking to retire and don&#8217;t have anyone to pass the business on to. Other times, this is just how entrepreneurs work. &#8220;If they make $5 million in a sale to Elevate, they will keep back $4 million for themselves, and use $1 million to start their next business,&#8221; he said.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"LIw8kaGel1\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/26/e-commerce-roll-ups-present-the-next-wave-of-disruption-in-consumer-packaged-goods/\">E-commerce roll-ups are the next wave of disruption in consumer packaged goods</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;E-commerce roll-ups are the next wave of disruption in consumer packaged goods&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/26/e-commerce-roll-ups-present-the-next-wave-of-disruption-in-consumer-packaged-goods/embed/#?secret=LIw8kaGel1\" data-secret=\"LIw8kaGel1\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>As for target companies, Elevate right now doesn&#8217;t focus on any specific product categories as other roll-up players might, although that may change in the future as the company gets more focused. What is a priority, however, is intellectual property &#8212; which to me is notable, given what sometimes feels like a genuine lack of differentiation when you look for products on Amazon.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We have preferences for businesses with patents, since those tend to be more differentiated,&#8221; he said. From there, it goes to those that have strong traction and brand pull. &#8220;When a product is doing well on Amazon, there is an enormous amount of data there, and so you tend to have copycats. We look for business that can maintain a competitive position, adding new variations and taking that to other marketplaces. And all of that is important in the building of communities. If you can build it that gives you an additional competitive advantage.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Acquisition valuations vary, he added, but on average are around four times a company&#8217;s EBITDA, but might go as high as five times or as low as 2.5x, depending on how competitive bidding is. Elevated&#8217;s acquisitions typically are already making between $2 million and $3 million in sellers&#8217; discretionary earnings, he added.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 02:35:19","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","title":"Gembah raises $11M to ‘democratize product innovation’","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2174863","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Gembah’s mission statement is a deceptively simple one. The Austin-based company says it’s looking to “democratize product innovation by drastically lowering barriers to entry for creation of new products.” In that respect, at least, it’s not so dissimilar from various startup initiatives that have arrived over the past decade, from crowdfunding to additive manufacturing.</p>\n<p>The company’s product is a platform/marketplace designed to guide users through the product-creation process, promising results in “as little as 90 days.” The forum connects smaller businesses to factories, supply chain experts, designers, engineers, etc. to help speed up the process. Just ask anyone who has attempted to launch a hardware startup &#8212; these things can be massively difficult to navigate.</p>\n<p>To help accelerate its own vision, <a href=\"https://gembah.com/\">Gembah</a> has raised an $11 million Series A, led by local firm ATX Venture Partners along with Silverton, Flexport, Brett Hurt, Jim Curry and Dan Graham.</p><div year, bringing its total funding up to $14.75 million.</p>\n<p>The company says the pandemic has actually been something of a boon for its business model, as hardware startups are looking toward a more online model &#8212; and something a bit closer to home than the traditional sales channels. The company says its revenue grew 500% in 2020 and is on track to triple revenues this year. It&#8217;s impressive growth in the face of some major supply chain issues that have impacted the industry during the past year and a half.</p>\n<p>It currently has 300 active customers, though it was yet to achieve profitability &#8212; hence the new round. “Since most of our customers are e-commerce companies we benefited from the accelerated growth of e-commerce,” CEO and co-founder Henrik Johansson tells TechCrunch. “Supply chains have been impacted to some degree, but as the global supply chain gets more complex and many companies want to diversify outside of China, they need help to navigate that change, and Gembah can help with that transition.”</p>\n<p>The funding will go toward increasing the company’s engineering team. At present, Gembah has 55 employees in the U.S., and 19 in other locations, including Asia and Mexico. The new headcount will be focused on growing the marketplace, supply chain workflow and machine-learning capabilities. Gembah will also look to grow its global network and make additional hires in marketing and UI/UX.</p>\n<p>“Gembah is a true innovator poised to help businesses capitalize on the growth of global eCommerce,” ATX Venture Partners&#8217; Chris Shonk said in a statement. “The Gembah marketplace promises to unlock virtually unlimited entrepreneurial equity by enabling a whole new breed of creators to enter the market.”</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"LhObVh1L0w\"><p><a 02:35:19","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","title":"Android 12 will let you play games before they finish downloading","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2176165","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">At its Game Developer Summit, Google today announced a new feature for Android game developers today that will speed up the time from starting a download in the Google Play store to the game launching by almost 2x &#8212; at least on Android 12 devices. The name of the new feature, &#8216;play as you download,&#8217; pretty much gives away what this is all about. Even before all the game&#8217;s assets have been downloaded, players will be able to get going.</p>\n<p>On average, modern games are likely the largest apps you&#8217;ll ever download and when that download takes a couple of minutes, you may have long moved on to the next TikTok session before the game is ever ready to play. With this new feature, Google promises that it&#8217;ll take only half the time to jump into a game that weighs in at 400MB or so. If you&#8217;re a console gamer, this whole concept will also feel familiar, given that Sony pretty much does the same thing for PlayStation games.</p>\n<p>Now, this isn&#8217;t Google&#8217;s first attempt at making games load faster. With &#8216;<a href=\"https://developer.android.com/topic/google-play-instant\">Google Play Instant</a>,&#8217; the company already offers a related feature that allows gamers to immediately start a game from the Play Store. The idea there, though, is to completely do away with the install process and give potential players an opportunity to try out a new game right away.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Like Play Instant, the new &#8216;play as you download&#8217; feature is powered by Google&#8217;s <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/06/the-future-of-android-app-bundles-is.html\">Android App Bundle format,</a> which is, for the most part, replacing the old APK standard</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2176169\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a 02:35:19","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","title":"Twitter appoints resident grievance officer in India to comply with new internet rules","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2175890","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Twitter has appointed a resident grievance officer in India days after the American social media firm said to have <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/06/twitter-has-lost-liability-protection-in-india-government-says/\">lost the liability protection</a> on user-generated content in the South Asian nation over non-compliance with local IT rules.</p>\n<p>On Sunday, Twitter <a href=\"https://help.twitter.com/en/rules-and-policies/report-twitter-abuse-india\">identified</a> Vinay Prakash as its new resident grievance officer and shared a way to contact him as required by India’s new IT rules, which was unveiled in February this year and went into effect in late May. Twitter has also published a compliance report, another requirement listed in the new rules.</p>\n<p>Earlier this week, the Indian government had told a local court that Twitter had lost the liability protection on user-generated content in the country, as it had failed to appoint compliance, grievance and a so-called nodal contact officials to address on-ground concerns.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Other internet giants including Facebook, Google, and Telegram have already appointed these local compliance officers in India.</p>\n<p>Internet services enjoy what is broadly referred to as “safe harbor” protection that say that tech platforms won’t be held liable for the things their users post or share online. If you insult someone on Twitter, for instance, the company may be asked to take down your post (if the person you have insulted has approached the court and a takedown order has been issued) but it likely won’t be held legally responsible for what you said or did.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"JkLoOjJkwG\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/05/24/delhi-police-run-by-indias-central-government-raids-twitter-offices-over-manipulated-label/\">Police in India visited Twitter offices over &#8216;manipulated media&#8217; label</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Police in India visited Twitter offices over &#8216;manipulated media&#8217; label&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/05/24/delhi-police-run-by-indias-central-government-raids-twitter-offices-over-manipulated-label/embed/#?secret=JkLoOjJkwG\" data-secret=\"JkLoOjJkwG\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Without the protection, Twitter — which according to mobile insight firm App Annie, has over 100 million users in India — is on paper responsible for everything those users say on its platform. Indian police have already filed at least five cases against the company or its officials in the country over a range of issues.</p>\n<p>The new development should help assuage the tension between Twitter and the Indian government. A special squad of Delhi police <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/05/24/delhi-police-run-by-indias-central-government-raids-twitter-offices-over-manipulated-label/\">made a surprise visit to two of Twitter’s offices</a> in late May in what many perceived as an intimidation tactic. Twitter said at the time that it was “concerned by recent events regarding our employees in India and the potential threat to freedom of expression for the people we serve” and requested the Indian government to grant it three additional months to comply with the new IT rules.</p>\n<p>Earlier this week, Twitter told an Indian court that it was working to &#8220;fully comply&#8221; with the new rules.</p>\n<p>More countries are formulating similar requirements for tech giants in their nations. Russia President Vladimir Putin signed a law that mandates foreign social media giants to open offices in Russia. Any social firm with a daily user base of 500,000 people or more is required to comply with the new law.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" 02:35:19","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:19","title":"Microsoft confirms it’s buying cybersecurity startup RiskIQ","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2176145","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Microsoft has confirmed it&#8217;s buying <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/riskiq/\">RiskIQ</a>, a San Francisco-based cybersecurity company that provides threat intelligence and cloud-based software as a service for organizations.</p>\n<p>Terms of the deal, which will see RiskIQ&#8217;s threat intelligence services integrated into Microsoft&#8217;s flagship security offerings, were not disclosed, although <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-07-11/microsoft-is-said-to-be-buying-cybersecurity-company-riskiq?sref=BAcrnccI\">Bloomberg</a> previously reported that Microsoft will pay more than $500 million in cash for the company. Microsoft declined to confirm the reported figure.</p>\n<p>The announcement comes amid a heightened security landscape as organizations shift to remote and hybrid working strategies.</p>\n<p>RiskIQ scours the web, mapping out details about websites and networks, domain name records, certificates and other information, like WHOIS registration data, providing customers visibility into what assets, devices and services can be accessed outside of a company&#8217;s firewall. That helps companies lock down their assets and limit their attack surface from malicious actors. It&#8217;s that data in large part that helped the company <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/11/13/magecart-hackers-persistent-credit-card-skimmer-groups/\">discover and understand Magecart</a>, a collection of groups that inject credit card stealing malware into vulnerable websites.</p>\n<p>Microsoft says that by embedding RiskIQ&#8217;s technologies into its core products, its customers will be able to build a more comprehensive view of the global threats to their businesses as workforces continue to work outside of the traditional office environment.</p>\n<p>The deal will also help organizations to keep an eye on supply-chain risks, Microsoft says. This is likely a growing priority for many: an attack on software provider SolarWinds last year saw affected at least 18,000 of its customers, and just this month IT vendor <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/05/kaseya-hack-flood-ransomware/\">Kaseya fell victim to a ransomware attack</a> that spread to more than 1,000 downstream businesses.</p>\n<p>Eric Doerr, vice president of cloud security at Microsoft, said: &#8220;RiskIQ helps customers discover and assess the security of their entire enterprise attack surface — <wbr></wbr>in the Microsoft cloud, AWS, other clouds, on-premises, and from their supply chain. With more than a decade of experience scanning and analyzing the internet, RiskIQ can help enterprises identify and remediate vulnerable assets before an attacker can capitalize on them.&#8221;</p>\n<p>RiskIQ was founded in 2009 and has raised a total of $83 million over four rounds of funding. Elias Manousos, who co-founded RiskIQ and serves as its chief executive, said he was &#8220;thrilled&#8221; at the acquisition.</p>\n<p>“The vision and mission of RiskIQ is to provide unmatched internet visibility and insights to better protect and inform our customers and partners’ security programs,&#8221; said Manousos. &#8220;Our combined capabilities will enable best-in-class protection, investigations, and response against today’s threats.”</p>\n<p>The acquisition is one of many Microsoft has made recently in the cybersecurity space in recent months. The software giant last year <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/06/22/microsoft-confirms-acquisition-of-cyberx-to-boost-security-in-its-iot-business/\">bought Israeli security startup CyberX in a bid to boost its Azure IoT business, </a>and just last month it acquired Internet of Things security firm ReFirm Labs.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"nXvokP3lpf\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/07/12/equity-monday-cybersecurity-startups-see-deluge-of-capital-as-microsoft-looks-to-buy-riskiq/\">Equity Monday: Cybersecurity
